\DoxyCodeLine{797 }
\DoxyCodeLine{798 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{799 \textcolor{comment}{Least squares fitting report. This structure contains informational fields}}
\DoxyCodeLine{800 \textcolor{comment}{which are set by fitting functions provided by this unit.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{801 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{802 \textcolor{comment}{Different functions initialize different sets of  fields,  so  you  should}}
\DoxyCodeLine{803 \textcolor{comment}{read documentation on specific function you used in order  to  know  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{804 \textcolor{comment}{fields are initialized.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{805 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{806 \textcolor{comment}{    TaskRCond       reciprocal of task's condition number}}
\DoxyCodeLine{807 \textcolor{comment}{    IterationsCount number of internal iterations}}
\DoxyCodeLine{808 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{809 \textcolor{comment}{    VarIdx          if user-\/supplied gradient contains errors  which  were}}
\DoxyCodeLine{810 \textcolor{comment}{                    detected by nonlinear fitter, this  field  is  set  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{811 \textcolor{comment}{                    index  of  the  first  component  of gradient which is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{812 \textcolor{comment}{                    suspected to be spoiled by bugs.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{813 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{814 \textcolor{comment}{    RMSError        RMS error}}
\DoxyCodeLine{815 \textcolor{comment}{    AvgError        average error}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1332 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1333 \textcolor{comment}{Rational interpolant without poles}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1334 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1335 \textcolor{comment}{The subroutine constructs the rational interpolating function without real}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1336 \textcolor{comment}{poles  (see  'Barycentric rational interpolation with no  poles  and  high}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1337 \textcolor{comment}{rates of approximation', Michael S. Floater. and  Kai  Hormann,  for  more}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1338 \textcolor{comment}{information on this subject).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1339 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1340 \textcolor{comment}{Input parameters:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1341 \textcolor{comment}{    X   -\/   interpolation nodes, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1342 \textcolor{comment}{    Y   -\/   function values, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1343 \textcolor{comment}{    N   -\/   number of nodes, N>0.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1344 \textcolor{comment}{    D   -\/   order of the interpolation scheme, 0 <= D <= N-\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1345 \textcolor{comment}{            D<0 will cause an error.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1346 \textcolor{comment}{            D>=N it will be replaced with D=N-\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1347 \textcolor{comment}{            if you don't know what D to choose, use small value about 3-\/5.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1348 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1349 \textcolor{comment}{Output parameters:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1350 \textcolor{comment}{    B   -\/   barycentric interpolant.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1351 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1352 \textcolor{comment}{Note:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1353 \textcolor{comment}{    this algorithm always succeeds and calculates the weights  with  close}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1354 \textcolor{comment}{    to machine precision.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1355 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1356 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1357 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 17.06.2007 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1358 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1363 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1364 \textcolor{comment}{This function serializes data structure to string.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1365 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1366 \textcolor{comment}{Important properties of s\_out:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1367 \textcolor{comment}{* it contains alphanumeric characters, dots, underscores, minus signs}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1368 \textcolor{comment}{* these symbols are grouped into words, which are separated by spaces}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1369 \textcolor{comment}{  and Windows-\/style (CR+LF) newlines}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1370 \textcolor{comment}{* although  serializer  uses  spaces and CR+LF as separators, you can }}
\DoxyCodeLine{1371 \textcolor{comment}{  replace any separator character by arbitrary combination of spaces,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1372 \textcolor{comment}{  tabs, Windows or Unix newlines. It allows flexible reformatting  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1373 \textcolor{comment}{  the  string  in  case you want to include it into text or XML file. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{1374 \textcolor{comment}{  But you should not insert separators into the middle of the "{}words"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1375 \textcolor{comment}{  nor you should change case of letters.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1376 \textcolor{comment}{* s\_out can be freely moved between 32-\/bit and 64-\/bit systems, little}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1377 \textcolor{comment}{  and big endian machines, and so on. You can serialize structure  on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1378 \textcolor{comment}{  32-\/bit machine and unserialize it on 64-\/bit one (or vice versa), or}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1379 \textcolor{comment}{  serialize  it  on  SPARC  and  unserialize  on  x86.  You  can also }}
\DoxyCodeLine{1380 \textcolor{comment}{  serialize  it  in  C++ version of ALGLIB and unserialize in C\# one, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{1381 \textcolor{comment}{  and vice versa.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1382 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1413 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1414 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1415 \textcolor{comment}{This function creates buffer  structure  which  can  be  used  to  perform}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1416 \textcolor{comment}{parallel  IDW  model  evaluations  (with  one  IDW  model  instance  being}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1417 \textcolor{comment}{used from multiple threads, as long as  different  threads  use  different}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1418 \textcolor{comment}{instances of buffer).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1419 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1420 \textcolor{comment}{This buffer object can be used with  idwtscalcbuf()  function  (here  "{}ts"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1421 \textcolor{comment}{stands for "{}thread-\/safe"{}, "{}buf"{} is a suffix which denotes  function  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1422 \textcolor{comment}{reuses previously allocated output space).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1423 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1424 \textcolor{comment}{How to use it:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1425 \textcolor{comment}{* create IDW model structure or load it from file}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1426 \textcolor{comment}{* call idwcreatecalcbuffer(), once per thread working with IDW model  (you}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1427 \textcolor{comment}{  should call this function only AFTER model initialization, see below for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1428 \textcolor{comment}{  more information)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1429 \textcolor{comment}{* call idwtscalcbuf() from different threads,  with  each  thread  working}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1430 \textcolor{comment}{  with its own copy of buffer object.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1431 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1432 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1433 \textcolor{comment}{    S           -\/   IDW model}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1434 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1435 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1436 \textcolor{comment}{    Buf         -\/   external buffer.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1437 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1438 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1439 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: buffer object should be used only with  IDW model object  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1440 \textcolor{comment}{           was used to initialize buffer. Any attempt to use buffer   with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1441 \textcolor{comment}{           different object is dangerous -\/ you may  get  memory  violation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1442 \textcolor{comment}{           error because sizes of internal arrays do not fit to dimensions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1443 \textcolor{comment}{           of the IDW structure.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1444 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1445 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: you  should  call  this function only for model which was built}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1446 \textcolor{comment}{           with model builder (or unserialized from file). Sizes  of  some}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1447 \textcolor{comment}{           internal structures are determined only after model  is  built,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1448 \textcolor{comment}{           so buffer object created before model construction  stage  will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1449 \textcolor{comment}{           be useless (and any attempt to use it will result in exception).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1450 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1451 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1452 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 22.10.2018 by Sergey Bochkanov}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1453 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1454 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} idwcreatecalcbuffer(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1idwmodel}{idwmodel}} \&s, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1idwcalcbuffer}{idwcalcbuffer}} \&buf, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{1457 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1458 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine creates builder object used  to  generate IDW  model  from}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1459 \textcolor{comment}{irregularly sampled (scattered) dataset.  Multidimensional  scalar/vector-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1460 \textcolor{comment}{-\/valued are supported.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1461 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1462 \textcolor{comment}{Builder object is used to fit model to data as follows:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1463 \textcolor{comment}{* builder object is created with idwbuildercreate() function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1464 \textcolor{comment}{* dataset is added with idwbuildersetpoints() function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1465 \textcolor{comment}{* one of the modern IDW algorithms is chosen with either:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1466 \textcolor{comment}{  * idwbuildersetalgomstab()            -\/ Multilayer STABilized algorithm (interpolation)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1467 \textcolor{comment}{  Alternatively, one of the textbook algorithms can be chosen (not recommended):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1468 \textcolor{comment}{  * idwbuildersetalgotextbookshepard()  -\/ textbook Shepard algorithm}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1469 \textcolor{comment}{  * idwbuildersetalgotextbookmodshepard()-\/textbook modified Shepard algorithm}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1470 \textcolor{comment}{* finally, model construction is performed with idwfit() function.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1471 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1472 \textcolor{comment}{  ! COMMERCIAL EDITION OF ALGLIB:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1473 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1474 \textcolor{comment}{  ! Commercial Edition of ALGLIB includes following important improvements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1475 \textcolor{comment}{  ! of this function:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1476 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * high-\/performance native backend with same C\# interface (C\# version)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1477 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * multithreading support (C++ and C\# versions)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1478 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1479 \textcolor{comment}{  ! We recommend you to read 'Working with commercial version' section  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1480 \textcolor{comment}{  ! ALGLIB Reference Manual in order to find out how to  use  performance-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1481 \textcolor{comment}{  ! related features provided by commercial edition of ALGLIB.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1482 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1483 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1484 \textcolor{comment}{    NX  -\/   dimensionality of the argument, NX>=1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1485 \textcolor{comment}{    NY  -\/   dimensionality of the function being modeled, NY>=1;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1486 \textcolor{comment}{            NY=1 corresponds to classic scalar function, NY>=1 corresponds}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1487 \textcolor{comment}{            to vector-\/valued function.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1488 \textcolor{comment}{}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1492 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1498 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1499 \textcolor{comment}{This function changes number of layers used by IDW-\/MSTAB algorithm.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1500 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1501 \textcolor{comment}{The more layers you have, the finer details can  be  reproduced  with  IDW}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1502 \textcolor{comment}{model. The less layers you have, the less memory and CPU time is  consumed}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1503 \textcolor{comment}{by the model.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1504 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1505 \textcolor{comment}{Memory consumption grows linearly with layers count,  running  time  grows}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1506 \textcolor{comment}{sub-\/linearly.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1507 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1508 \textcolor{comment}{The default number of layers is 16, which allows you to reproduce  details}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1509 \textcolor{comment}{at distance down to SRad/65536. You will rarely need to change it.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1510 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1511 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1512 \textcolor{comment}{    State   -\/   builder object}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1513 \textcolor{comment}{    NLayers -\/   NLayers>=1, the number of layers used by the model.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1514 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1515 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1516 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 22.10.2018 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1517 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1542 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1543 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1544 \textcolor{comment}{This function sets IDW model  construction  algorithm  to  the  Multilayer}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1545 \textcolor{comment}{Stabilized IDW method (IDW-\/MSTAB), a  latest  incarnation  of  the inverse}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1546 \textcolor{comment}{distance weighting interpolation which fixes shortcomings of  the original}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1547 \textcolor{comment}{and modified Shepard's variants.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1548 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1549 \textcolor{comment}{The distinctive features of IDW-\/MSTAB are:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1550 \textcolor{comment}{1) exact interpolation  is  pursued  (as  opposed  to  fitting  and  noise}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1551 \textcolor{comment}{   suppression)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1552 \textcolor{comment}{2) improved robustness when compared with that of other algorithms:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1553 \textcolor{comment}{   * MSTAB shows almost no strange  fitting  artifacts  like  ripples  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1554 \textcolor{comment}{     sharp spikes (unlike N-\/dimensional splines and HRBFs)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1555 \textcolor{comment}{   * MSTAB does not return function values far from the  interval  spanned}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1556 \textcolor{comment}{     by the dataset; say, if all your points have |f|<=1, you  can be sure}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1557 \textcolor{comment}{     that model value won't deviate too much from [-\/1,+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1558 \textcolor{comment}{3) good model construction time competing with that of HRBFs  and  bicubic}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1559 \textcolor{comment}{   splines}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1560 \textcolor{comment}{4) ability to work with any number of dimensions, starting from NX=1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1561 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1562 \textcolor{comment}{The drawbacks of IDW-\/MSTAB (and all IDW algorithms in general) are:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1563 \textcolor{comment}{1) dependence of the model evaluation time on the search radius}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1564 \textcolor{comment}{2) bad extrapolation properties, models built by this method  are  usually}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1565 \textcolor{comment}{   conservative in their predictions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1566 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1567 \textcolor{comment}{Thus, IDW-\/MSTAB is  a  good  "{}default"{}  option  if  you  want  to  perform}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1568 \textcolor{comment}{scattered multidimensional interpolation. Although it has  its  drawbacks,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1569 \textcolor{comment}{it is easy to use and robust, which makes it a good first step.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1570 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1571 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1572 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1573 \textcolor{comment}{    State   -\/   builder object}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1574 \textcolor{comment}{    SRad    -\/   initial search radius, SRad>0 is required. A model  value}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1575 \textcolor{comment}{                is obtained by "{}smart"{} averaging  of  the  dataset  points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1576 \textcolor{comment}{                within search radius.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1577 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1578 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 1: IDW interpolation can  correctly  handle  ANY  dataset,  including}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1579 \textcolor{comment}{        datasets with non-\/distinct points. In case non-\/distinct points are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1580 \textcolor{comment}{        found, an average value for this point will be calculated.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1581 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1582 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 2: the memory requirements for model storage are O(NPoints*NLayers).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1583 \textcolor{comment}{        The model construction needs twice as much memory as model storage.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1584 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1585 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 3: by default 16 IDW layers are built which is enough for most cases.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1586 \textcolor{comment}{        You can change this parameter with idwbuildersetnlayers()  method.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1587 \textcolor{comment}{        Larger values may be necessary if you need to reproduce  extrafine}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1588 \textcolor{comment}{        details at distances smaller than SRad/65536.  Smaller value   may}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1589 \textcolor{comment}{        be necessary if you have to save memory and  computing  time,  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1590 \textcolor{comment}{        ready to sacrifice some model quality.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1591 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1592 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1593 \textcolor{comment}{ALGORITHM DESCRIPTION}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1594 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1595 \textcolor{comment}{ALGLIB implementation of IDW is somewhat similar to the modified Shepard's}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1596 \textcolor{comment}{method (one with search radius R) but overcomes several of its  drawbacks,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1597 \textcolor{comment}{namely:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1598 \textcolor{comment}{1) a tendency to show stepwise behavior for uniform datasets}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1599 \textcolor{comment}{2) a tendency to show terrible interpolation properties for highly}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1600 \textcolor{comment}{   nonuniform datasets which often arise in geospatial tasks}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1601 \textcolor{comment}{  (function values are densely sampled across multiple separated}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1602 \textcolor{comment}{  "{}tracks"{})}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1603 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1604 \textcolor{comment}{IDW-\/MSTAB method performs several passes over dataset and builds a sequence}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1605 \textcolor{comment}{of progressively refined IDW models  (layers),  which starts from one with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1606 \textcolor{comment}{largest search radius SRad  and continues to smaller  search  radii  until}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1607 \textcolor{comment}{required number of  layers  is  built.  Highest  layers  reproduce  global}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1608 \textcolor{comment}{behavior of the target function at larger distances  whilst  lower  layers}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1609 \textcolor{comment}{reproduce fine details at smaller distances.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1610 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1611 \textcolor{comment}{Each layer is an IDW model built with following modifications:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1612 \textcolor{comment}{* weights go to zero when distance approach to the current search radius}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1613 \textcolor{comment}{* an additional regularizing term is added to the distance: w=1/(d\string^2+lambda)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1614 \textcolor{comment}{* an additional fictional term with unit weight and zero function value is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1615 \textcolor{comment}{  added in order to promote continuity  properties  at  the  isolated  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1616 \textcolor{comment}{  boundary points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1617 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1618 \textcolor{comment}{By default, 16 layers is built, which is enough for most  cases.  You  can}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1619 \textcolor{comment}{change this parameter with idwbuildersetnlayers() method.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1620 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1621 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1622 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 22.10.2018 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1623 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1624 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} idwbuildersetalgomstab(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1idwbuilder}{idwbuilder}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} srad, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{1625 }

\DoxyCodeLine{1640 \textcolor{comment}{        found, an average value for this point will be calculated.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1641 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1642 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1805 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1806 \textcolor{comment}{This function calculates values of the IDW model at the given point.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1807 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1808 \textcolor{comment}{Same as idwcalc(), but does not reallocate Y when in is large enough to}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1813 \textcolor{comment}{      evaluation from the multiple threads, use idwtscalcbuf()  with  per-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1814 \textcolor{comment}{      thread buffer object.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1815 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1816 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1817 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   IDW model}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1818 \textcolor{comment}{    X       -\/   coordinates, array[NX]. X may have more than NX  elements,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1819 \textcolor{comment}{                in this case only leading NX will be used.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1820 \textcolor{comment}{    Y       -\/   possibly preallocated array}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1887 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1888 \textcolor{comment}{Conversion from barycentric representation to Chebyshev basis.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1889 \textcolor{comment}{This function has O(N\string^2) complexity.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1890 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1891 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1892 \textcolor{comment}{    P   -\/   polynomial in barycentric form}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1893 \textcolor{comment}{    A,B -\/   base interval for Chebyshev polynomials (see below)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1894 \textcolor{comment}{            A<>B}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1895 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1896 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1897 \textcolor{comment}{    T   -\/   coefficients of Chebyshev representation;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1898 \textcolor{comment}{            P(x) = sum \{ T[i]*Ti(2*(x-\/A)/(B-\/A)-\/1), i=0..N-\/1 \},}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1899 \textcolor{comment}{            where Ti -\/ I-\/th Chebyshev polynomial.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1900 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1901 \textcolor{comment}{NOTES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1902 \textcolor{comment}{    barycentric interpolant passed as P may be either polynomial  obtained}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1903 \textcolor{comment}{    from  polynomial  interpolation/ fitting or rational function which is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1904 \textcolor{comment}{    NOT polynomial. We can't distinguish between these two cases, and this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1905 \textcolor{comment}{    algorithm just tries to work assuming that P IS a polynomial.  If not,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1906 \textcolor{comment}{    algorithm will return results, but they won't have any meaning.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1907 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1908 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1909 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 30.09.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1910 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1911 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} polynomialbar2cheb(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1barycentricinterpolant}{barycentricinterpolant}} \&p, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} a, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} b, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&t, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{1912 }

\DoxyCodeLine{1914 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1915 \textcolor{comment}{Conversion from Chebyshev basis to barycentric representation.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1916 \textcolor{comment}{This function has O(N\string^2) complexity.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1917 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1918 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1919 \textcolor{comment}{    T   -\/   coefficients of Chebyshev representation;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1920 \textcolor{comment}{            P(x) = sum \{ T[i]*Ti(2*(x-\/A)/(B-\/A)-\/1), i=0..N \},}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1921 \textcolor{comment}{            where Ti -\/ I-\/th Chebyshev polynomial.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1922 \textcolor{comment}{    N   -\/   number of coefficients:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1923 \textcolor{comment}{            * if given, only leading N elements of T are used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1924 \textcolor{comment}{            * if not given, automatically determined from size of T}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1925 \textcolor{comment}{    A,B -\/   base interval for Chebyshev polynomials (see above)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1926 \textcolor{comment}{            A<B}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1927 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1928 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1929 \textcolor{comment}{    P   -\/   polynomial in barycentric form}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1930 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1931 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1932 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 30.09.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1933 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1934 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} polynomialcheb2bar(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&t, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} a, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} b, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1barycentricinterpolant}{barycentricinterpolant}} \&p, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{1937 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1938 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1939 \textcolor{comment}{Conversion from barycentric representation to power basis.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1940 \textcolor{comment}{This function has O(N\string^2) complexity.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1941 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1942 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1943 \textcolor{comment}{    P   -\/   polynomial in barycentric form}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1944 \textcolor{comment}{    C   -\/   offset (see below); 0.0 is used as default value.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1945 \textcolor{comment}{    S   -\/   scale (see below);  1.0 is used as default value. S<>0.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1946 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1947 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1948 \textcolor{comment}{    A   -\/   coefficients, P(x) = sum \{ A[i]*((X-\/C)/S)\string^i, i=0..N-\/1 \}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1949 \textcolor{comment}{    N   -\/   number of coefficients (polynomial degree plus 1)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1950 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1951 \textcolor{comment}{NOTES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1952 \textcolor{comment}{1.  this function accepts offset and scale, which can be  set  to  improve}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1953 \textcolor{comment}{    numerical properties of polynomial. For example, if P was obtained  as}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1954 \textcolor{comment}{    result of interpolation on [-\/1,+1],  you  can  set  C=0  and  S=1  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1955 \textcolor{comment}{    represent  P  as sum of 1, x, x\string^2, x\string^3 and so on. In most cases you it}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1956 \textcolor{comment}{    is exactly what you need.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1957 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1958 \textcolor{comment}{    However, if your interpolation model was built on [999,1001], you will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1959 \textcolor{comment}{    see significant growth of numerical errors when using \{1, x, x\string^2, x\string^3\}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1960 \textcolor{comment}{    as basis. Representing P as sum of 1, (x-\/1000), (x-\/1000)\string^2, (x-\/1000)\string^3}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1961 \textcolor{comment}{    will be better option. Such representation can be  obtained  by  using}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1962 \textcolor{comment}{    1000.0 as offset C and 1.0 as scale S.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1963 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1964 \textcolor{comment}{2.  power basis is ill-\/conditioned and tricks described above can't  solve}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1965 \textcolor{comment}{    this problem completely. This function  will  return  coefficients  in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1966 \textcolor{comment}{    any  case,  but  for  N>8  they  will  become unreliable. However, N's}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1967 \textcolor{comment}{    less than 5 are pretty safe.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1968 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1969 \textcolor{comment}{3.  barycentric interpolant passed as P may be either polynomial  obtained}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1970 \textcolor{comment}{    from  polynomial  interpolation/ fitting or rational function which is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1971 \textcolor{comment}{    NOT polynomial. We can't distinguish between these two cases, and this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1972 \textcolor{comment}{    algorithm just tries to work assuming that P IS a polynomial.  If not,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1973 \textcolor{comment}{    algorithm will return results, but they won't have any meaning.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1974 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1975 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1976 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 30.09.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1977 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1978 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} polynomialbar2pow(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1barycentricinterpolant}{barycentricinterpolant}} \&p, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} s, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&a, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{1979 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} polynomialbar2pow(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1barycentricinterpolant}{barycentricinterpolant}} \&p, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&a, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{1980 }

\DoxyCodeLine{1984 \textcolor{comment}{This function has O(N\string^2) complexity.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1985 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1986 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}

\DoxyCodeLine{1991 \textcolor{comment}{    C   -\/   offset (see below); 0.0 is used as default value.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2005 \textcolor{comment}{    see significant growth of numerical errors when using \{1, x, x\string^2, x\string^3\}}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2009 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2010 \textcolor{comment}{2.  power basis is ill-\/conditioned and tricks described above can't  solve}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2012 \textcolor{comment}{    in any case, but for N>8 accuracy well degrade. However, N's less than}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2013 \textcolor{comment}{    5 are pretty safe.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2203 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2204 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine builds linear spline interpolant}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2211 \textcolor{comment}{            * if given, only first N points are used to build spline}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2222 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2223 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2224 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 24.06.2007 by Bochkanov Sergey}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2228 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2229 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2230 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2231 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine builds cubic spline interpolant.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2232 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2233 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2234 \textcolor{comment}{    X           -\/   spline nodes, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2235 \textcolor{comment}{    Y           -\/   function values, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2236 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2237 \textcolor{comment}{OPTIONAL PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2238 \textcolor{comment}{    N           -\/   points count:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2239 \textcolor{comment}{                    * N>=2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2240 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if given, only first N points are used to build spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2241 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if not given, automatically detected from X/Y sizes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2242 \textcolor{comment}{                      (len(X) must be equal to len(Y))}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2243 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundLType  -\/   boundary condition type for the left boundary}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2244 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundL      -\/   left boundary condition (first or second derivative,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2245 \textcolor{comment}{                    depending on the BoundLType)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2246 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundRType  -\/   boundary condition type for the right boundary}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2247 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundR      -\/   right boundary condition (first or second derivative,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2248 \textcolor{comment}{                    depending on the BoundRType)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2249 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2250 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2251 \textcolor{comment}{    C           -\/   spline interpolant}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2252 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2253 \textcolor{comment}{ORDER OF POINTS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2254 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2255 \textcolor{comment}{Subroutine automatically sorts points, so caller may pass unsorted array.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2256 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2257 \textcolor{comment}{SETTING BOUNDARY VALUES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2258 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2259 \textcolor{comment}{The BoundLType/BoundRType parameters can have the following values:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2260 \textcolor{comment}{    * -\/1, which corresonds to the periodic (cyclic) boundary conditions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2261 \textcolor{comment}{          In this case:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2262 \textcolor{comment}{          * both BoundLType and BoundRType must be equal to -\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2263 \textcolor{comment}{          * BoundL/BoundR are ignored}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2264 \textcolor{comment}{          * Y[last] is ignored (it is assumed to be equal to Y[first]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2265 \textcolor{comment}{    *  0, which  corresponds  to  the  parabolically   terminated  spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2266 \textcolor{comment}{          (BoundL and/or BoundR are ignored).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2267 \textcolor{comment}{    *  1, which corresponds to the first derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2268 \textcolor{comment}{    *  2, which corresponds to the second derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2269 \textcolor{comment}{    *  by default, BoundType=0 is used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2270 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2271 \textcolor{comment}{PROBLEMS WITH PERIODIC BOUNDARY CONDITIONS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2272 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2273 \textcolor{comment}{Problems with periodic boundary conditions have Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2274 \textcolor{comment}{However, this subroutine doesn't require you to specify equal  values  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2275 \textcolor{comment}{the first and last points -\/ it automatically forces them  to  be  equal by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2276 \textcolor{comment}{copying  Y[first\_point]  (corresponds  to the leftmost,  minimal  X[])  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2277 \textcolor{comment}{Y[last\_point]. However it is recommended to pass consistent values of Y[],}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2278 \textcolor{comment}{i.e. to make Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2279 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2280 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2281 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 23.06.2007 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2282 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2283 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline1dbuildcubic(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t boundltype, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} boundl, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t boundrtype, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} boundr, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dinterpolant}{spline1dinterpolant}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{2284 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline1dbuildcubic(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dinterpolant}{spline1dinterpolant}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{2285 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2286 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2287 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2288 \textcolor{comment}{This function solves following problem: given table y[] of function values}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2289 \textcolor{comment}{at nodes x[], it calculates and returns table of function derivatives  d[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2290 \textcolor{comment}{(calculated at the same nodes x[]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2291 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2292 \textcolor{comment}{This function yields same result as Spline1DBuildCubic() call followed  by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2293 \textcolor{comment}{sequence of Spline1DDiff() calls, but it can be several times faster  when}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2294 \textcolor{comment}{called for ordered X[] and X2[].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2295 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2296 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2297 \textcolor{comment}{    X           -\/   spline nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2298 \textcolor{comment}{    Y           -\/   function values}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2299 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2300 \textcolor{comment}{OPTIONAL PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2301 \textcolor{comment}{    N           -\/   points count:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2302 \textcolor{comment}{                    * N>=2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2303 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if given, only first N points are used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2304 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if not given, automatically detected from X/Y sizes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2305 \textcolor{comment}{                      (len(X) must be equal to len(Y))}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2306 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundLType  -\/   boundary condition type for the left boundary}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2307 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundL      -\/   left boundary condition (first or second derivative,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2308 \textcolor{comment}{                    depending on the BoundLType)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2309 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundRType  -\/   boundary condition type for the right boundary}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2310 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundR      -\/   right boundary condition (first or second derivative,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2311 \textcolor{comment}{                    depending on the BoundRType)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2312 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2313 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2314 \textcolor{comment}{    D           -\/   derivative values at X[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2315 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2316 \textcolor{comment}{ORDER OF POINTS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2317 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2318 \textcolor{comment}{Subroutine automatically sorts points, so caller may pass unsorted array.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2319 \textcolor{comment}{Derivative values are correctly reordered on return, so  D[I]  is  always}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2320 \textcolor{comment}{equal to S'(X[I]) independently of points order.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2321 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2322 \textcolor{comment}{SETTING BOUNDARY VALUES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2323 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2324 \textcolor{comment}{The BoundLType/BoundRType parameters can have the following values:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2325 \textcolor{comment}{    * -\/1, which corresonds to the periodic (cyclic) boundary conditions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2326 \textcolor{comment}{          In this case:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2327 \textcolor{comment}{          * both BoundLType and BoundRType must be equal to -\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2328 \textcolor{comment}{          * BoundL/BoundR are ignored}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2329 \textcolor{comment}{          * Y[last] is ignored (it is assumed to be equal to Y[first]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2330 \textcolor{comment}{    *  0, which  corresponds  to  the  parabolically   terminated  spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2331 \textcolor{comment}{          (BoundL and/or BoundR are ignored).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2332 \textcolor{comment}{    *  1, which corresponds to the first derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2333 \textcolor{comment}{    *  2, which corresponds to the second derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2334 \textcolor{comment}{    *  by default, BoundType=0 is used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2335 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2336 \textcolor{comment}{PROBLEMS WITH PERIODIC BOUNDARY CONDITIONS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2337 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2338 \textcolor{comment}{Problems with periodic boundary conditions have Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2339 \textcolor{comment}{However, this subroutine doesn't require you to specify equal  values  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2340 \textcolor{comment}{the first and last points -\/ it automatically forces them  to  be  equal by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2341 \textcolor{comment}{copying  Y[first\_point]  (corresponds  to the leftmost,  minimal  X[])  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2342 \textcolor{comment}{Y[last\_point]. However it is recommended to pass consistent values of Y[],}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2343 \textcolor{comment}{i.e. to make Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2344 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2345 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2346 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 03.09.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2347 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2353 \textcolor{comment}{This function solves following problem: given table y[] of function values}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2354 \textcolor{comment}{at  nodes  x[],  it  calculates  and  returns  tables  of first and second}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2355 \textcolor{comment}{function derivatives d1[] and d2[] (calculated at the same nodes x[]).}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2380 \textcolor{comment}{    D2          -\/   S'' values at X[]}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2393 \textcolor{comment}{          * both BoundLType and BoundRType must be equal to -\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2394 \textcolor{comment}{          * BoundL/BoundR are ignored}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2395 \textcolor{comment}{          * Y[last] is ignored (it is assumed to be equal to Y[first]).}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2403 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2404 \textcolor{comment}{Problems with periodic boundary conditions have Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2405 \textcolor{comment}{However, this subroutine doesn't require you to specify equal  values  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2406 \textcolor{comment}{the first and last points -\/ it automatically forces them  to  be  equal by}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2515 \textcolor{comment}{                    * N2>=2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2516 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if given, only first N2 points from X2 are used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2517 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if not given, automatically detected from X2 size}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2518 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2519 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2520 \textcolor{comment}{    F2          -\/   function values at X2[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2521 \textcolor{comment}{    D2          -\/   first derivatives at X2[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2522 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2523 \textcolor{comment}{ORDER OF POINTS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2524 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2525 \textcolor{comment}{Subroutine automatically sorts points, so caller  may pass unsorted array.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2526 \textcolor{comment}{Function  values  are correctly reordered on  return, so F2[I]  is  always}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2527 \textcolor{comment}{equal to S(X2[I]) independently of points order.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2528 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2529 \textcolor{comment}{SETTING BOUNDARY VALUES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2530 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2531 \textcolor{comment}{The BoundLType/BoundRType parameters can have the following values:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2532 \textcolor{comment}{    * -\/1, which corresonds to the periodic (cyclic) boundary conditions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2533 \textcolor{comment}{          In this case:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2534 \textcolor{comment}{          * both BoundLType and BoundRType must be equal to -\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2535 \textcolor{comment}{          * BoundL/BoundR are ignored}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2536 \textcolor{comment}{          * Y[last] is ignored (it is assumed to be equal to Y[first]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2537 \textcolor{comment}{    *  0, which  corresponds  to  the  parabolically   terminated  spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2538 \textcolor{comment}{          (BoundL and/or BoundR are ignored).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2539 \textcolor{comment}{    *  1, which corresponds to the first derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2540 \textcolor{comment}{    *  2, which corresponds to the second derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2541 \textcolor{comment}{    *  by default, BoundType=0 is used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2542 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2543 \textcolor{comment}{PROBLEMS WITH PERIODIC BOUNDARY CONDITIONS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2544 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2545 \textcolor{comment}{Problems with periodic boundary conditions have Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2546 \textcolor{comment}{However, this subroutine doesn't require you to specify equal  values  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2547 \textcolor{comment}{the first and last points -\/ it automatically forces them  to  be  equal by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2548 \textcolor{comment}{copying  Y[first\_point]  (corresponds  to the leftmost,  minimal  X[])  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2549 \textcolor{comment}{Y[last\_point]. However it is recommended to pass consistent values of Y[],}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2550 \textcolor{comment}{i.e. to make Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2551 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2552 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2553 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 03.09.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2554 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2555 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline1dconvdiffcubic(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t boundltype, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} boundl, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t boundrtype, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} boundr, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x2, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n2, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y2, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&d2, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{2556 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline1dconvdiffcubic(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x2, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y2, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&d2, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{2558 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2559 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2560 \textcolor{comment}{This function solves following problem: given table y[] of function values}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2561 \textcolor{comment}{at old nodes x[]  and new nodes  x2[],  it calculates and returns table of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2562 \textcolor{comment}{function  values  y2[],  first  and  second  derivatives  d2[]  and  dd2[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2563 \textcolor{comment}{(calculated at x2[]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2564 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2565 \textcolor{comment}{This function yields same result as Spline1DBuildCubic() call followed  by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2566 \textcolor{comment}{sequence of Spline1DDiff() calls, but it can be several times faster  when}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2567 \textcolor{comment}{called for ordered X[] and X2[].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2568 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2569 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2570 \textcolor{comment}{    X           -\/   old spline nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2571 \textcolor{comment}{    Y           -\/   function values}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2572 \textcolor{comment}{    X2           -\/  new spline nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2573 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2574 \textcolor{comment}{OPTIONAL PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2575 \textcolor{comment}{    N           -\/   points count:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2576 \textcolor{comment}{                    * N>=2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2577 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if given, only first N points from X/Y are used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2578 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if not given, automatically detected from X/Y sizes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2579 \textcolor{comment}{                      (len(X) must be equal to len(Y))}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2580 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundLType  -\/   boundary condition type for the left boundary}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2581 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundL      -\/   left boundary condition (first or second derivative,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2582 \textcolor{comment}{                    depending on the BoundLType)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2583 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundRType  -\/   boundary condition type for the right boundary}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2584 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundR      -\/   right boundary condition (first or second derivative,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2585 \textcolor{comment}{                    depending on the BoundRType)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2586 \textcolor{comment}{    N2          -\/   new points count:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2587 \textcolor{comment}{                    * N2>=2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2588 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if given, only first N2 points from X2 are used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2589 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if not given, automatically detected from X2 size}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2590 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2591 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2592 \textcolor{comment}{    F2          -\/   function values at X2[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2593 \textcolor{comment}{    D2          -\/   first derivatives at X2[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2594 \textcolor{comment}{    DD2         -\/   second derivatives at X2[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2595 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2596 \textcolor{comment}{ORDER OF POINTS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2597 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2598 \textcolor{comment}{Subroutine automatically sorts points, so caller  may pass unsorted array.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2599 \textcolor{comment}{Function  values  are correctly reordered on  return, so F2[I]  is  always}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2600 \textcolor{comment}{equal to S(X2[I]) independently of points order.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2601 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2602 \textcolor{comment}{SETTING BOUNDARY VALUES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2603 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2604 \textcolor{comment}{The BoundLType/BoundRType parameters can have the following values:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2605 \textcolor{comment}{    * -\/1, which corresonds to the periodic (cyclic) boundary conditions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2606 \textcolor{comment}{          In this case:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2607 \textcolor{comment}{          * both BoundLType and BoundRType must be equal to -\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2608 \textcolor{comment}{          * BoundL/BoundR are ignored}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2609 \textcolor{comment}{          * Y[last] is ignored (it is assumed to be equal to Y[first]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2610 \textcolor{comment}{    *  0, which  corresponds  to  the  parabolically   terminated  spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2611 \textcolor{comment}{          (BoundL and/or BoundR are ignored).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2612 \textcolor{comment}{    *  1, which corresponds to the first derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2613 \textcolor{comment}{    *  2, which corresponds to the second derivative boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2614 \textcolor{comment}{    *  by default, BoundType=0 is used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2615 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2616 \textcolor{comment}{PROBLEMS WITH PERIODIC BOUNDARY CONDITIONS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2617 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2618 \textcolor{comment}{Problems with periodic boundary conditions have Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2619 \textcolor{comment}{However, this subroutine doesn't require you to specify equal  values  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2620 \textcolor{comment}{the first and last points -\/ it automatically forces them  to  be  equal by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2621 \textcolor{comment}{copying  Y[first\_point]  (corresponds  to the leftmost,  minimal  X[])  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2622 \textcolor{comment}{Y[last\_point]. However it is recommended to pass consistent values of Y[],}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2623 \textcolor{comment}{i.e. to make Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2624 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2625 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2626 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 03.09.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2632 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2633 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine builds Catmull-\/Rom spline interpolant.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2634 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2635 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2636 \textcolor{comment}{    X           -\/   spline nodes, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2637 \textcolor{comment}{    Y           -\/   function values, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2638 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2639 \textcolor{comment}{OPTIONAL PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2640 \textcolor{comment}{    N           -\/   points count:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2641 \textcolor{comment}{                    * N>=2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2642 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if given, only first N points are used to build spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2643 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if not given, automatically detected from X/Y sizes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2644 \textcolor{comment}{                      (len(X) must be equal to len(Y))}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2645 \textcolor{comment}{    BoundType   -\/   boundary condition type:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2646 \textcolor{comment}{                    * -\/1 for periodic boundary condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2647 \textcolor{comment}{                    *  0 for parabolically terminated spline (default)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2648 \textcolor{comment}{    Tension     -\/   tension parameter:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2649 \textcolor{comment}{                    * tension=0   corresponds to classic Catmull-\/Rom spline (default)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2650 \textcolor{comment}{                    * 0<tension<1 corresponds to more general form -\/ cardinal spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2651 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2652 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2653 \textcolor{comment}{    C           -\/   spline interpolant}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2654 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2655 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2656 \textcolor{comment}{ORDER OF POINTS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2657 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2658 \textcolor{comment}{Subroutine automatically sorts points, so caller may pass unsorted array.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2659 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2660 \textcolor{comment}{PROBLEMS WITH PERIODIC BOUNDARY CONDITIONS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2661 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2662 \textcolor{comment}{Problems with periodic boundary conditions have Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2663 \textcolor{comment}{However, this subroutine doesn't require you to specify equal  values  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2664 \textcolor{comment}{the first and last points -\/ it automatically forces them  to  be  equal by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2665 \textcolor{comment}{copying  Y[first\_point]  (corresponds  to the leftmost,  minimal  X[])  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2666 \textcolor{comment}{Y[last\_point]. However it is recommended to pass consistent values of Y[],}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2667 \textcolor{comment}{i.e. to make Y[first\_point]=Y[last\_point].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2668 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2669 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2731 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2732 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine calculates the value of the spline at the given point X.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2733 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2734 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2735 \textcolor{comment}{    C   -\/   spline interpolant}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2736 \textcolor{comment}{    X   -\/   point}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2737 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2738 \textcolor{comment}{Result:}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2767 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2768 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2774 \textcolor{comment}{            For I = 0...N-\/2:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2775 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[I,0] = X[i]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2776 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[I,1] = X[i+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2777 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[I,2] = C0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2778 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[I,3] = C1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2779 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[I,4] = C2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2780 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[I,5] = C3}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2781 \textcolor{comment}{            On [x[i], x[i+1]] spline is equals to:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2782 \textcolor{comment}{                S(x) = C0 + C1*t + C2*t\string^2 + C3*t\string^3}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2783 \textcolor{comment}{                t = x-\/x[i]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2784 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2785 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2786 \textcolor{comment}{    You  can rebuild spline with  Spline1DBuildHermite()  function,  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2787 \textcolor{comment}{    accepts as inputs function values and derivatives at nodes, which  are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2788 \textcolor{comment}{    easy to calculate when you have coefficients.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2789 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2790 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2791 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 29.06.2007 by Bochkanov Sergey}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2841 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2842 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2843 \textcolor{comment}{Fitting by smoothing (penalized) cubic spline.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2844 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2845 \textcolor{comment}{This function approximates N scattered points (some of X[] may be equal to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2846 \textcolor{comment}{each other) by cubic spline with M  nodes  at  equidistant  grid  spanning}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2847 \textcolor{comment}{interval [min(x,xc),max(x,xc)].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2848 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2849 \textcolor{comment}{The problem is regularized by adding nonlinearity penalty to  usual  least}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2850 \textcolor{comment}{squares penalty function:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2851 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2852 \textcolor{comment}{    MERIT\_FUNC = F\_LS + F\_NL}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2853 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2854 \textcolor{comment}{where F\_LS is a least squares error  term,  and  F\_NL  is  a  nonlinearity}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2855 \textcolor{comment}{penalty which is roughly proportional to LambdaNS*integral\{ S''(x)\string^2*dx \}.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2856 \textcolor{comment}{Algorithm applies automatic renormalization of F\_NL  which  makes  penalty}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2857 \textcolor{comment}{term roughly invariant to scaling of X[] and changes in M.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2858 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2859 \textcolor{comment}{This function is a new edition  of  penalized  regression  spline fitting,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2860 \textcolor{comment}{a fast and compact one which needs much less resources that  its  previous}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2861 \textcolor{comment}{version: just O(maxMN) memory and O(maxMN*log(maxMN)) time.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2862 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2863 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: it is OK to run this function with both M<<N and M>>N;  say,  it  is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2864 \textcolor{comment}{      possible to process 100 points with 1000-\/node spline.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2865 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2866 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2867 \textcolor{comment}{    X           -\/   points, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2868 \textcolor{comment}{    Y           -\/   function values, array[0..N-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2869 \textcolor{comment}{    N           -\/   number of points (optional):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2870 \textcolor{comment}{                    * N>0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2871 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if given, only first N elements of X/Y are processed}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2872 \textcolor{comment}{                    * if not given, automatically determined from lengths}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2873 \textcolor{comment}{    M           -\/   number of basis functions ( = number\_of\_nodes), M>=4.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2874 \textcolor{comment}{    LambdaNS    -\/   LambdaNS>=0, regularization  constant  passed by user.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2875 \textcolor{comment}{                    It penalizes nonlinearity in the regression spline.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2876 \textcolor{comment}{                    Possible values to start from are 0.00001, 0.1, 1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2877 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2878 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2879 \textcolor{comment}{    S   -\/   spline interpolant.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2880 \textcolor{comment}{    Rep -\/   Following fields are set:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2881 \textcolor{comment}{            * RMSError      rms error on the (X,Y).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2882 \textcolor{comment}{            * AvgError      average error on the (X,Y).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2883 \textcolor{comment}{            * AvgRelError   average relative error on the non-\/zero Y}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2884 \textcolor{comment}{            * MaxError      maximum error}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2885 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2886 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2887 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 27.08.2019 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2888 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2889 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline1dfit(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t m, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} lambdans, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dinterpolant}{spline1dinterpolant}} \&s, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dfitreport}{spline1dfitreport}} \&rep, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{2890 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline1dfit(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t m, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} lambdans, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dinterpolant}{spline1dinterpolant}} \&s, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dfitreport}{spline1dfitreport}} \&rep, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{2891 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2892 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2893 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2894 \textcolor{comment}{This function builds monotone cubic Hermite interpolant. This interpolant}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2895 \textcolor{comment}{is monotonic in [x(0),x(n-\/1)] and is constant outside of this interval.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2896 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2897 \textcolor{comment}{In  case  y[]  form  non-\/monotonic  sequence,  interpolant  is  piecewise}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2898 \textcolor{comment}{monotonic.  Say, for x=(0,1,2,3,4)  and  y=(0,1,2,1,0)  interpolant  will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2899 \textcolor{comment}{monotonically grow at [0..2] and monotonically decrease at [2..4].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2900 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2901 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2902 \textcolor{comment}{    X           -\/   spline nodes, array[0..N-\/1]. Subroutine automatically}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2903 \textcolor{comment}{                    sorts points, so caller may pass unsorted array.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2904 \textcolor{comment}{    Y           -\/   function values, array[0..N-\/1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2905 \textcolor{comment}{    N           -\/   the number of points(N>=2).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2906 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2907 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2908 \textcolor{comment}{    C           -\/   spline interpolant.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2909 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2910 \textcolor{comment}{ -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2911 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 21.06.2012 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2912 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{2916 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2917 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#if defined(AE\_COMPILE\_LSFIT) || !defined(AE\_PARTIAL\_BUILD)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2918 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2919 \textcolor{comment}{This  subroutine fits piecewise linear curve to points with Ramer-\/Douglas-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2920 \textcolor{comment}{Peucker algorithm, which stops after generating specified number of linear}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2921 \textcolor{comment}{sections.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2922 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2923 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2924 \textcolor{comment}{* it does NOT perform least-\/squares fitting; it  builds  curve,  but  this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2925 \textcolor{comment}{  curve does not minimize some least squares metric.  See  description  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2926 \textcolor{comment}{  RDP algorithm (say, in Wikipedia) for more details on WHAT is performed.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2927 \textcolor{comment}{* this function does NOT work with parametric curves  (i.e.  curves  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2928 \textcolor{comment}{  can be represented as \{X(t),Y(t)\}. It works with curves   which  can  be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2929 \textcolor{comment}{  represented as Y(X). Thus,  it  is  impossible  to  model  figures  like}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2930 \textcolor{comment}{  circles  with  this  functions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2931 \textcolor{comment}{  If  you  want  to  work  with  parametric   curves,   you   should   use}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2932 \textcolor{comment}{  ParametricRDPFixed() function provided  by  "{}Parametric"{}  subpackage  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2933 \textcolor{comment}{  "{}Interpolation"{} package.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2934 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2935 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2936 \textcolor{comment}{    X       -\/   array of X-\/coordinates:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2937 \textcolor{comment}{                * at least N elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2938 \textcolor{comment}{                * can be unordered (points are automatically sorted)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2939 \textcolor{comment}{                * this function may accept non-\/distinct X (see below for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2940 \textcolor{comment}{                  more information on handling of such inputs)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2941 \textcolor{comment}{    Y       -\/   array of Y-\/coordinates:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2942 \textcolor{comment}{                * at least N elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2943 \textcolor{comment}{    N       -\/   number of elements in X/Y}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2944 \textcolor{comment}{    M       -\/   desired number of sections:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2945 \textcolor{comment}{                * at most M sections are generated by this function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2946 \textcolor{comment}{                * less than M sections can be generated if we have N<M}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2947 \textcolor{comment}{                  (or some X are non-\/distinct).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2948 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2949 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2950 \textcolor{comment}{    X2      -\/   X-\/values of corner points for piecewise approximation,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2951 \textcolor{comment}{                has length NSections+1 or zero (for NSections=0).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2952 \textcolor{comment}{    Y2      -\/   Y-\/values of corner points,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2953 \textcolor{comment}{                has length NSections+1 or zero (for NSections=0).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2954 \textcolor{comment}{    NSections-\/  number of sections found by algorithm, NSections<=M,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2955 \textcolor{comment}{                NSections can be zero for degenerate datasets}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2956 \textcolor{comment}{                (N<=1 or all X[] are non-\/distinct).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2957 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2958 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: X2/Y2 are ordered arrays, i.e. (X2[0],Y2[0]) is  a  first  point  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2959 \textcolor{comment}{      curve, (X2[NSection-\/1],Y2[NSection-\/1]) is the last point.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2960 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2961 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2962 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 02.10.2014 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2963 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2964 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lstfitpiecewiselinearrdpfixed(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t m, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x2, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y2, ae\_int\_t \&nsections, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{2965 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2966 }
\DoxyCodeLine{2967 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2968 \textcolor{comment}{This  subroutine fits piecewise linear curve to points with Ramer-\/Douglas-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2969 \textcolor{comment}{Peucker algorithm, which stops after achieving desired precision.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2970 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2971 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2972 \textcolor{comment}{* it performs non-\/least-\/squares fitting; it builds curve, but  this  curve}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2973 \textcolor{comment}{  does not minimize some least squares  metric.  See  description  of  RDP}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2974 \textcolor{comment}{  algorithm (say, in Wikipedia) for more details on WHAT is performed.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2975 \textcolor{comment}{* this function does NOT work with parametric curves  (i.e.  curves  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2976 \textcolor{comment}{  can be represented as \{X(t),Y(t)\}. It works with curves   which  can  be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2977 \textcolor{comment}{  represented as Y(X). Thus, it is impossible to model figures like circles}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2978 \textcolor{comment}{  with this functions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2979 \textcolor{comment}{  If  you  want  to  work  with  parametric   curves,   you   should   use}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2980 \textcolor{comment}{  ParametricRDPFixed() function provided  by  "{}Parametric"{}  subpackage  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2981 \textcolor{comment}{  "{}Interpolation"{} package.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2982 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2983 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2984 \textcolor{comment}{    X       -\/   array of X-\/coordinates:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2985 \textcolor{comment}{                * at least N elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2986 \textcolor{comment}{                * can be unordered (points are automatically sorted)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2987 \textcolor{comment}{                * this function may accept non-\/distinct X (see below for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2988 \textcolor{comment}{                  more information on handling of such inputs)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2989 \textcolor{comment}{    Y       -\/   array of Y-\/coordinates:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2990 \textcolor{comment}{                * at least N elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2991 \textcolor{comment}{    N       -\/   number of elements in X/Y}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2992 \textcolor{comment}{    Eps     -\/   positive number, desired precision.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2993 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2994 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2995 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2996 \textcolor{comment}{    X2      -\/   X-\/values of corner points for piecewise approximation,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2997 \textcolor{comment}{                has length NSections+1 or zero (for NSections=0).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2998 \textcolor{comment}{    Y2      -\/   Y-\/values of corner points,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2999 \textcolor{comment}{                has length NSections+1 or zero (for NSections=0).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3000 \textcolor{comment}{    NSections-\/  number of sections found by algorithm,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3001 \textcolor{comment}{                NSections can be zero for degenerate datasets}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3002 \textcolor{comment}{                (N<=1 or all X[] are non-\/distinct).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3003 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3004 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: X2/Y2 are ordered arrays, i.e. (X2[0],Y2[0]) is  a  first  point  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3005 \textcolor{comment}{      curve, (X2[NSection-\/1],Y2[NSection-\/1]) is the last point.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3006 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3007 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3008 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 02.10.2014 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{3009 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
