\DoxyCodeLine{5041 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5042 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5043 \textcolor{comment}{This function sets scaling coefficients for underlying optimizer.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5044 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5045 \textcolor{comment}{ALGLIB optimizers use scaling matrices to test stopping  conditions  (step}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5046 \textcolor{comment}{size and gradient are scaled before comparison with tolerances).  Scale of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5047 \textcolor{comment}{the I-\/th variable is a translation invariant measure of:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5048 \textcolor{comment}{a) "{}how large"{} the variable is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5049 \textcolor{comment}{b) how large the step should be to make significant changes in the function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5050 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5051 \textcolor{comment}{Generally, scale is NOT considered to be a form of preconditioner.  But LM}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5052 \textcolor{comment}{optimizer is unique in that it uses scaling matrix both  in  the  stopping}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5053 \textcolor{comment}{condition tests and as Marquardt damping factor.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5054 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5055 \textcolor{comment}{Proper scaling is very important for the algorithm performance. It is less}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5056 \textcolor{comment}{important for the quality of results, but still has some influence (it  is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5057 \textcolor{comment}{easier  to  converge  when  variables  are  properly  scaled, so premature}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5058 \textcolor{comment}{stopping is possible when very badly scalled variables are  combined  with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5059 \textcolor{comment}{relaxed stopping conditions).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5060 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5061 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5062 \textcolor{comment}{    State   -\/   structure stores algorithm state}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5063 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   array[N], non-\/zero scaling coefficients}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5064 \textcolor{comment}{                S[i] may be negative, sign doesn't matter.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5065 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5066 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5067 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 14.01.2011 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5068 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5069 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitsetscale(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5070 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5071 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5072 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5073 \textcolor{comment}{This function sets boundary constraints for underlying optimizer}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5074 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5075 \textcolor{comment}{Boundary constraints are inactive by default (after initial creation).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5076 \textcolor{comment}{They are preserved until explicitly turned off with another SetBC() call.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5077 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5078 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5079 \textcolor{comment}{    State   -\/   structure stores algorithm state}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5080 \textcolor{comment}{    BndL    -\/   lower bounds, array[K].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5081 \textcolor{comment}{                If some (all) variables are unbounded, you may specify}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5082 \textcolor{comment}{                very small number or -\/INF (latter is recommended because}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5083 \textcolor{comment}{                it will allow solver to use better algorithm).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5084 \textcolor{comment}{    BndU    -\/   upper bounds, array[K].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5085 \textcolor{comment}{                If some (all) variables are unbounded, you may specify}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5086 \textcolor{comment}{                very large number or +INF (latter is recommended because}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5087 \textcolor{comment}{                it will allow solver to use better algorithm).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5088 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5089 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 1: it is possible to specify BndL[i]=BndU[i]. In this case I-\/th}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5090 \textcolor{comment}{variable will be "{}frozen"{} at X[i]=BndL[i]=BndU[i].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5091 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5092 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 2: unlike other constrained optimization algorithms, this solver  has}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5093 \textcolor{comment}{following useful properties:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5094 \textcolor{comment}{* bound constraints are always satisfied exactly}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5095 \textcolor{comment}{* function is evaluated only INSIDE area specified by bound constraints}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5096 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5097 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5098 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 14.01.2011 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5099 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5100 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitsetbc(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&bndl, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&bndu, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5101 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5102 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5103 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5104 \textcolor{comment}{This function sets linear constraints for underlying optimizer}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5105 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5106 \textcolor{comment}{Linear constraints are inactive by default (after initial creation).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5107 \textcolor{comment}{They are preserved until explicitly turned off with another SetLC() call.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5108 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5109 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5110 \textcolor{comment}{    State   -\/   structure stores algorithm state}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5111 \textcolor{comment}{    C       -\/   linear constraints, array[K,N+1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5112 \textcolor{comment}{                Each row of C represents one constraint, either equality}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5113 \textcolor{comment}{                or inequality (see below):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5114 \textcolor{comment}{                * first N elements correspond to coefficients,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5115 \textcolor{comment}{                * last element corresponds to the right part.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5116 \textcolor{comment}{                All elements of C (including right part) must be finite.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5117 \textcolor{comment}{    CT      -\/   type of constraints, array[K]:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5118 \textcolor{comment}{                * if CT[i]>0, then I-\/th constraint is C[i,*]*x >= C[i,n+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5119 \textcolor{comment}{                * if CT[i]=0, then I-\/th constraint is C[i,*]*x  = C[i,n+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5120 \textcolor{comment}{                * if CT[i]<0, then I-\/th constraint is C[i,*]*x <= C[i,n+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5121 \textcolor{comment}{    K       -\/   number of equality/inequality constraints, K>=0:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5122 \textcolor{comment}{                * if given, only leading K elements of C/CT are used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5123 \textcolor{comment}{                * if not given, automatically determined from sizes of C/CT}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5124 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5125 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: if you have linear constraints, it is strongly  recommended  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5126 \textcolor{comment}{           set scale of variables with lsfitsetscale(). QP solver which is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5127 \textcolor{comment}{           used to calculate linearly constrained steps heavily relies  on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5128 \textcolor{comment}{           good scaling of input problems.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5129 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5130 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: linear  (non-\/box)  constraints  are  satisfied only approximately  -\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5131 \textcolor{comment}{      there  always  exists some violation due  to  numerical  errors  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5132 \textcolor{comment}{      algorithmic limitations.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5133 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5134 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: general linear constraints  add  significant  overhead  to  solution}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5135 \textcolor{comment}{      process. Although solver performs roughly same amount of  iterations}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5136 \textcolor{comment}{      (when compared  with  similar  box-\/only  constrained  problem), each}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5137 \textcolor{comment}{      iteration   now    involves  solution  of  linearly  constrained  QP}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5138 \textcolor{comment}{      subproblem, which requires \string~3-\/5 times more Cholesky  decompositions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5139 \textcolor{comment}{      Thus, if you can reformulate your problem in such way  this  it  has}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5140 \textcolor{comment}{      only box constraints, it may be beneficial to do so.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5141 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5142 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5143 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 29.04.2017 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5144 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5145 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitsetlc(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1integer__1d__array}{integer\_1d\_array}} \&ct, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t k, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5146 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitsetlc(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1integer__1d__array}{integer\_1d\_array}} \&ct, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5147 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5148 }

\DoxyCodeLine{5151 \textcolor{comment}{Reverse communication interface is not documented or recommended to use.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5152 \textcolor{comment}{See below for functions which provide better documented API}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5153 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5154 \textcolor{keywordtype}{bool} lsfititeration(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5155 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5156 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5157 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5158 \textcolor{comment}{This family of functions is used to launcn iterations of nonlinear fitter}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5159 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5160 \textcolor{comment}{These functions accept following parameters:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5161 \textcolor{comment}{    state   -\/   algorithm state}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5162 \textcolor{comment}{    func    -\/   callback which calculates function (or merit function)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5163 \textcolor{comment}{                value func at given point x}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5164 \textcolor{comment}{    grad    -\/   callback which calculates function (or merit function)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5165 \textcolor{comment}{                value func and gradient grad at given point x}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5166 \textcolor{comment}{    hess    -\/   callback which calculates function (or merit function)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5167 \textcolor{comment}{                value func, gradient grad and Hessian hess at given point x}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5168 \textcolor{comment}{    rep     -\/   optional callback which is called after each iteration}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5169 \textcolor{comment}{                can be NULL}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5170 \textcolor{comment}{    ptr     -\/   optional pointer which is passed to func/grad/hess/jac/rep}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5171 \textcolor{comment}{                can be NULL}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5172 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5173 \textcolor{comment}{NOTES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5174 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5175 \textcolor{comment}{1. this algorithm is somewhat unusual because it works with  parameterized}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5176 \textcolor{comment}{   function f(C,X), where X is a function argument (we  have  many  points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5177 \textcolor{comment}{   which are characterized by different  argument  values),  and  C  is  a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5178 \textcolor{comment}{   parameter to fit.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5179 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5180 \textcolor{comment}{   For example, if we want to do linear fit by f(c0,c1,x) = c0*x+c1,  then}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5181 \textcolor{comment}{   x will be argument, and \{c0,c1\} will be parameters.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5182 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5183 \textcolor{comment}{   It is important to understand that this algorithm finds minimum in  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5184 \textcolor{comment}{   space of function PARAMETERS (not arguments), so it  needs  derivatives}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5185 \textcolor{comment}{   of f() with respect to C, not X.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5186 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5187 \textcolor{comment}{   In the example above it will need f=c0*x+c1 and \{df/dc0,df/dc1\} = \{x,1\}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5188 \textcolor{comment}{   instead of \{df/dx\} = \{c0\}.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5189 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5190 \textcolor{comment}{2. Callback functions accept C as the first parameter, and X as the second}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5191 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5192 \textcolor{comment}{3. If  state  was  created  with  LSFitCreateFG(),  algorithm  needs  just}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5193 \textcolor{comment}{   function   and   its   gradient,   but   if   state   was  created with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5194 \textcolor{comment}{   LSFitCreateFGH(), algorithm will need function, gradient and Hessian.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5195 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5196 \textcolor{comment}{   According  to  the  said  above,  there  ase  several  versions of this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5197 \textcolor{comment}{   function, which accept different sets of callbacks.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5198 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5199 \textcolor{comment}{   This flexibility opens way to subtle errors -\/ you may create state with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5200 \textcolor{comment}{   LSFitCreateFGH() (optimization using Hessian), but call function  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5201 \textcolor{comment}{   does not accept Hessian. So when algorithm will request Hessian,  there}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5202 \textcolor{comment}{   will be no callback to call. In this case exception will be thrown.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5203 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5204 \textcolor{comment}{   Be careful to avoid such errors because there is no way to find them at}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5205 \textcolor{comment}{   compile time -\/ you can see them at runtime only.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5206 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5207 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5208 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 17.08.2009 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5209 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5210 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5211 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitfit(\mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5212     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} (*func)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&func, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr),}

\DoxyCodeLine{5214     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr = NULL,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5215     \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5216 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitfit(\mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5217     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} (*func)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&func, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr),}
\DoxyCodeLine{5218     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} (*grad)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&func, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&grad, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr),}
\DoxyCodeLine{5219     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void}  (*rep)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} func, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr) = NULL,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5220     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr = NULL,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5221     \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5222 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitfit(\mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5223     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} (*func)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&func, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr),}
\DoxyCodeLine{5224     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} (*grad)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&func, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&grad, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr),}
\DoxyCodeLine{5225     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} (*hess)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&func, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&grad, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&hess, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr),}
\DoxyCodeLine{5226     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void}  (*rep)(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} func, \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr) = NULL,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5227     \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} *ptr = NULL,}
\DoxyCodeLine{5228     \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5229 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5230 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5231 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5232 \textcolor{comment}{Nonlinear least squares fitting results.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5233 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5234 \textcolor{comment}{Called after return from LSFitFit().}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5235 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5236 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5237 \textcolor{comment}{    State   -\/   algorithm state}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5238 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5239 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5240 \textcolor{comment}{    Info    -\/   completion code:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5241 \textcolor{comment}{                    * -\/8    optimizer   detected  NAN/INF  in  the  target}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5242 \textcolor{comment}{                            function and/or gradient}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5243 \textcolor{comment}{                    * -\/7    gradient verification failed.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5244 \textcolor{comment}{                            See LSFitSetGradientCheck() for more information.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5245 \textcolor{comment}{                    * -\/3    inconsistent constraints}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5246 \textcolor{comment}{                    *  2    relative step is no more than EpsX.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5247 \textcolor{comment}{                    *  5    MaxIts steps was taken}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5248 \textcolor{comment}{                    *  7    stopping conditions are too stringent,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5249 \textcolor{comment}{                            further improvement is impossible}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5250 \textcolor{comment}{    C       -\/   array[0..K-\/1], solution}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5251 \textcolor{comment}{    Rep     -\/   optimization report. On success following fields are set:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5252 \textcolor{comment}{                * R2                non-\/adjusted coefficient of determination}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5253 \textcolor{comment}{                                    (non-\/weighted)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5254 \textcolor{comment}{                * RMSError          rms error on the (X,Y).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5255 \textcolor{comment}{                * AvgError          average error on the (X,Y).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5256 \textcolor{comment}{                * AvgRelError       average relative error on the non-\/zero Y}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5257 \textcolor{comment}{                * MaxError          maximum error}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5258 \textcolor{comment}{                                    NON-\/WEIGHTED ERRORS ARE CALCULATED}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5259 \textcolor{comment}{                * WRMSError         weighted rms error on the (X,Y).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5260 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5261 \textcolor{comment}{ERRORS IN PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5262 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5263 \textcolor{comment}{This  solver  also  calculates different kinds of errors in parameters and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5264 \textcolor{comment}{fills corresponding fields of report:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5265 \textcolor{comment}{* Rep.CovPar        covariance matrix for parameters, array[K,K].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5266 \textcolor{comment}{* Rep.ErrPar        errors in parameters, array[K],}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5267 \textcolor{comment}{                    errpar = sqrt(diag(CovPar))}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5268 \textcolor{comment}{* Rep.ErrCurve      vector of fit errors -\/ standard deviations of empirical}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5269 \textcolor{comment}{                    best-\/fit curve from "{}ideal"{} best-\/fit curve built  with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5270 \textcolor{comment}{                    infinite number of samples, array[N].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5271 \textcolor{comment}{                    errcurve = sqrt(diag(J*CovPar*J')),}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5272 \textcolor{comment}{                    where J is Jacobian matrix.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5273 \textcolor{comment}{* Rep.Noise         vector of per-\/point estimates of noise, array[N]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5274 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5275 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT:  errors  in  parameters  are  calculated  without  taking  into}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5276 \textcolor{comment}{            account boundary/linear constraints! Presence  of  constraints}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5277 \textcolor{comment}{            changes distribution of errors, but there is no  easy  way  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5278 \textcolor{comment}{            account for constraints when you calculate covariance matrix.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5279 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5280 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE:       noise in the data is estimated as follows:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5281 \textcolor{comment}{            * for fitting without user-\/supplied  weights  all  points  are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5282 \textcolor{comment}{              assumed to have same level of noise, which is estimated from}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5283 \textcolor{comment}{              the data}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5284 \textcolor{comment}{            * for fitting with user-\/supplied weights we assume that  noise}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5285 \textcolor{comment}{              level in I-\/th point is inversely proportional to Ith weight.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5286 \textcolor{comment}{              Coefficient of proportionality is estimated from the data.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5287 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5288 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE:       we apply small amount of regularization when we invert squared}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5289 \textcolor{comment}{            Jacobian and calculate covariance matrix. It  guarantees  that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5290 \textcolor{comment}{            algorithm won't divide by zero  during  inversion,  but  skews}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5291 \textcolor{comment}{            error estimates a bit (fractional error is about 10\string^-\/9).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5292 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5293 \textcolor{comment}{            However, we believe that this difference is insignificant  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5294 \textcolor{comment}{            all practical purposes except for the situation when you  want}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5295 \textcolor{comment}{            to compare ALGLIB results with "{}reference"{}  implementation  up}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5296 \textcolor{comment}{            to the last significant digit.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5297 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5298 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE:       covariance matrix is estimated using  correction  for  degrees}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5299 \textcolor{comment}{            of freedom (covariances are divided by N-\/M instead of dividing}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5300 \textcolor{comment}{            by N).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5301 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5302 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5303 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 17.08.2009 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5304 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5305 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitresults(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state, ae\_int\_t \&info, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&c, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitreport}{lsfitreport}} \&rep, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5306 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5307 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5308 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5309 \textcolor{comment}{This  subroutine  turns  on  verification  of  the  user-\/supplied analytic}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5310 \textcolor{comment}{gradient:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5311 \textcolor{comment}{* user calls this subroutine before fitting begins}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5312 \textcolor{comment}{* LSFitFit() is called}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5313 \textcolor{comment}{* prior to actual fitting, for  each  point  in  data  set  X\_i  and  each}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5314 \textcolor{comment}{  component  of  parameters  being  fited C\_j algorithm performs following}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5315 \textcolor{comment}{  steps:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5316 \textcolor{comment}{  * two trial steps are made to C\_j-\/TestStep*S[j] and C\_j+TestStep*S[j],}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5317 \textcolor{comment}{    where C\_j is j-\/th parameter and S[j] is a scale of j-\/th parameter}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5318 \textcolor{comment}{  * if needed, steps are bounded with respect to constraints on C[]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5319 \textcolor{comment}{  * F(X\_i|C) is evaluated at these trial points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5320 \textcolor{comment}{  * we perform one more evaluation in the middle point of the interval}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5321 \textcolor{comment}{  * we  build  cubic  model using function values and derivatives at trial}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5322 \textcolor{comment}{    points and we compare its prediction with actual value in  the  middle}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5323 \textcolor{comment}{    point}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5324 \textcolor{comment}{  * in case difference between prediction and actual value is higher  than}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5325 \textcolor{comment}{    some predetermined threshold, algorithm stops with completion code -\/7;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5326 \textcolor{comment}{    Rep.VarIdx is set to index of the parameter with incorrect derivative.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5327 \textcolor{comment}{* after verification is over, algorithm proceeds to the actual optimization.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5328 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5329 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 1: verification needs N*K (points count * parameters count)  gradient}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5330 \textcolor{comment}{        evaluations. It is very costly and you should use it only for  low}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5331 \textcolor{comment}{        dimensional  problems,  when  you  want  to  be  sure  that you've}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5332 \textcolor{comment}{        correctly calculated analytic derivatives. You should not  use  it}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5333 \textcolor{comment}{        in the production code  (unless  you  want  to  check  derivatives}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5334 \textcolor{comment}{        provided by some third party).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5335 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5336 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 2: you  should  carefully  choose  TestStep. Value which is too large}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5337 \textcolor{comment}{        (so large that function behaviour is significantly non-\/cubic) will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5338 \textcolor{comment}{        lead to false alarms. You may use  different  step  for  different}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5339 \textcolor{comment}{        parameters by means of setting scale with LSFitSetScale().}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5340 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5341 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 3: this function may lead to false positives. In case it reports that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5342 \textcolor{comment}{        I-\/th  derivative was calculated incorrectly, you may decrease test}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5343 \textcolor{comment}{        step  and  try  one  more  time  -\/ maybe your function changes too}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5344 \textcolor{comment}{        sharply  and  your  step  is  too  large for such rapidly chanding}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5345 \textcolor{comment}{        function.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5346 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5347 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 4: this function works only for optimizers created with LSFitCreateWFG()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5348 \textcolor{comment}{        or LSFitCreateFG() constructors.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5349 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5350 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5351 \textcolor{comment}{    State       -\/   structure used to store algorithm state}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5352 \textcolor{comment}{    TestStep    -\/   verification step:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5353 \textcolor{comment}{                    * TestStep=0 turns verification off}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5354 \textcolor{comment}{                    * TestStep>0 activates verification}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5355 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5356 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5357 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 15.06.2012 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5358 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5359 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} lsfitsetgradientcheck(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1lsfitstate}{lsfitstate}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} teststep, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5360 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#endif}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5361 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5362 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#if defined(AE\_COMPILE\_FITSPHERE) || !defined(AE\_PARTIAL\_BUILD)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5363 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5364 \textcolor{comment}{Fits least squares (LS) circle (or NX-\/dimensional sphere) to data  (a  set}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5365 \textcolor{comment}{of points in NX-\/dimensional space).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5366 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5367 \textcolor{comment}{Least squares circle minimizes sum of squared deviations between distances}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5368 \textcolor{comment}{from points to the center and  some  "{}candidate"{}  radius,  which  is  also}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5369 \textcolor{comment}{fitted to the data.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5370 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5371 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5372 \textcolor{comment}{    XY      -\/   array[NPoints,NX] (or larger), contains dataset.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5373 \textcolor{comment}{                One row = one point in NX-\/dimensional space.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5374 \textcolor{comment}{    NPoints -\/   dataset size, NPoints>0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5375 \textcolor{comment}{    NX      -\/   space dimensionality, NX>0 (1, 2, 3, 4, 5 and so on)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5376 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5377 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5378 \textcolor{comment}{    CX      -\/   central point for a sphere}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5379 \textcolor{comment}{    R       -\/   radius}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5380 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5381 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5382 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 07.05.2018 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5383 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5384 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} fitspherels(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&xy, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t npoints, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nx, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&cx, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&r, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5385 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5386 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5387 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5388 \textcolor{comment}{Fits minimum circumscribed (MC) circle (or NX-\/dimensional sphere) to  data}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5389 \textcolor{comment}{(a set of points in NX-\/dimensional space).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5390 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5391 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5392 \textcolor{comment}{    XY      -\/   array[NPoints,NX] (or larger), contains dataset.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5393 \textcolor{comment}{                One row = one point in NX-\/dimensional space.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5394 \textcolor{comment}{    NPoints -\/   dataset size, NPoints>0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5395 \textcolor{comment}{    NX      -\/   space dimensionality, NX>0 (1, 2, 3, 4, 5 and so on)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5396 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5397 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5398 \textcolor{comment}{    CX      -\/   central point for a sphere}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5399 \textcolor{comment}{    RHi     -\/   radius}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5400 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5401 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: this function is an easy-\/to-\/use wrapper around more powerful "{}expert"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5402 \textcolor{comment}{      function fitspherex().}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5403 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5404 \textcolor{comment}{      This  wrapper  is optimized  for  ease of use and stability -\/ at the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5405 \textcolor{comment}{      cost of somewhat lower  performance  (we  have  to  use  very  tight}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5406 \textcolor{comment}{      stopping criteria for inner optimizer because we want to  make  sure}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5407 \textcolor{comment}{      that it will converge on any dataset).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5408 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5409 \textcolor{comment}{      If you are ready to experiment with settings of  "{}expert"{}  function,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5410 \textcolor{comment}{      you can achieve \string~2-\/4x speedup over standard "{}bulletproof"{} settings.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5411 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5412 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5413 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5414 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 14.04.2017 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5415 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{5481 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} fitspheremz(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&xy, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t npoints, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nx, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&cx, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&rlo, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&rhi, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5482 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5483 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5484 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5485 \textcolor{comment}{Fitting minimum circumscribed, maximum inscribed or minimum  zone  circles}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5486 \textcolor{comment}{(or NX-\/dimensional spheres)  to  data  (a  set of points in NX-\/dimensional}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5487 \textcolor{comment}{space).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5488 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5489 \textcolor{comment}{This  is  expert  function  which  allows  to  tweak  many  parameters  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5490 \textcolor{comment}{underlying nonlinear solver:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5491 \textcolor{comment}{* stopping criteria for inner iterations}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5492 \textcolor{comment}{* number of outer iterations}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5493 \textcolor{comment}{* penalty coefficient used to handle  nonlinear  constraints  (we  convert}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5494 \textcolor{comment}{  unconstrained nonsmooth optimization problem ivolving max() and/or min()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5495 \textcolor{comment}{  operations to quadratically constrained smooth one).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5496 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5497 \textcolor{comment}{You may tweak all these parameters or only some  of  them,  leaving  other}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5498 \textcolor{comment}{ones at their default state -\/ just specify zero  value,  and  solver  will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5499 \textcolor{comment}{fill it with appropriate default one.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5500 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5501 \textcolor{comment}{These comments also include some discussion of  approach  used  to  handle}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5502 \textcolor{comment}{such unusual fitting problem,  its  stability,  drawbacks  of  alternative}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5503 \textcolor{comment}{methods, and convergence properties.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5504 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5505 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5506 \textcolor{comment}{    XY      -\/   array[NPoints,NX] (or larger), contains dataset.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5507 \textcolor{comment}{                One row = one point in NX-\/dimensional space.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5508 \textcolor{comment}{    NPoints -\/   dataset size, NPoints>0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5509 \textcolor{comment}{    NX      -\/   space dimensionality, NX>0 (1, 2, 3, 4, 5 and so on)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5510 \textcolor{comment}{    ProblemType-\/used to encode problem type:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5511 \textcolor{comment}{                * 0 for least squares circle}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5512 \textcolor{comment}{                * 1 for minimum circumscribed circle/sphere fitting (MC)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5513 \textcolor{comment}{                * 2 for  maximum inscribed circle/sphere fitting (MI)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5514 \textcolor{comment}{                * 3 for minimum zone circle fitting (difference between}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5515 \textcolor{comment}{                    Rhi and Rlo is minimized), denoted as MZ}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5516 \textcolor{comment}{    EpsX    -\/   stopping condition for NLC optimizer:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5517 \textcolor{comment}{                * must be non-\/negative}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5518 \textcolor{comment}{                * use 0 to choose default value (1.0E-\/12 is used by default)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5519 \textcolor{comment}{                * you may specify larger values, up to 1.0E-\/6, if you want}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5520 \textcolor{comment}{                  to   speed-\/up   solver;   NLC   solver  performs several}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5521 \textcolor{comment}{                  preconditioned  outer  iterations,   so   final   result}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5522 \textcolor{comment}{                  typically has precision much better than EpsX.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5523 \textcolor{comment}{    AULIts  -\/   number of outer iterations performed by NLC optimizer:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5524 \textcolor{comment}{                * must be non-\/negative}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5525 \textcolor{comment}{                * use 0 to choose default value (20 is used by default)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5526 \textcolor{comment}{                * you may specify values smaller than 20 if you want to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5527 \textcolor{comment}{                  speed up solver; 10 often results in good combination of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5528 \textcolor{comment}{                  precision and speed; sometimes you may get good results}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5529 \textcolor{comment}{                  with just 6 outer iterations.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5530 \textcolor{comment}{                Ignored for ProblemType=0.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5531 \textcolor{comment}{    Penalty -\/   penalty coefficient for NLC optimizer:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5532 \textcolor{comment}{                * must be non-\/negative}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5533 \textcolor{comment}{                * use 0 to choose default value (1.0E6 in current version)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5534 \textcolor{comment}{                * it should be really large, 1.0E6...1.0E7 is a good value}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5535 \textcolor{comment}{                  to start from;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5536 \textcolor{comment}{                * generally, default value is good enough}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5537 \textcolor{comment}{                Ignored for ProblemType=0.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5538 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5539 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5540 \textcolor{comment}{    CX      -\/   central point for a sphere}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5541 \textcolor{comment}{    RLo     -\/   radius:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5542 \textcolor{comment}{                * for ProblemType=2,3, radius of the inscribed sphere}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5543 \textcolor{comment}{                * for ProblemType=0 -\/ radius of the least squares sphere}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5544 \textcolor{comment}{                * for ProblemType=1 -\/ zero}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5545 \textcolor{comment}{    RHo     -\/   radius:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5546 \textcolor{comment}{                * for ProblemType=1,3, radius of the circumscribed sphere}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5547 \textcolor{comment}{                * for ProblemType=0 -\/ radius of the least squares sphere}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5548 \textcolor{comment}{                * for ProblemType=2 -\/ zero}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5549 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5550 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: ON THE UNIQUENESS OF SOLUTIONS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5551 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5552 \textcolor{comment}{ALGLIB provides solution to several related circle fitting  problems:   MC}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5553 \textcolor{comment}{(minimum circumscribed), MI (maximum inscribed)   and   MZ  (minimum zone)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5554 \textcolor{comment}{fitting, LS (least squares) fitting.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5555 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5556 \textcolor{comment}{It  is  important  to  note  that  among these problems only MC and LS are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5557 \textcolor{comment}{convex and have unique solution independently from starting point.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5558 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5559 \textcolor{comment}{As  for MI,  it  may (or  may  not, depending on dataset properties)  have}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5560 \textcolor{comment}{multiple solutions, and it always  has  one degenerate solution C=infinity}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5561 \textcolor{comment}{which corresponds to infinitely large radius. Thus, there are no guarantees}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5562 \textcolor{comment}{that solution to  MI returned by this solver will be the best one (and  no}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5563 \textcolor{comment}{one can provide you with such guarantee because problem is  NP-\/hard).  The}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5564 \textcolor{comment}{only guarantee you have is that this solution is locally optimal, i.e.  it}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5565 \textcolor{comment}{can not be improved by infinitesimally small tweaks in the parameters.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5566 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5567 \textcolor{comment}{It  is  also  possible  to "{}run away"{} to infinity when  started  from  bad}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5568 \textcolor{comment}{initial point located outside of point cloud (or when point cloud does not}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5569 \textcolor{comment}{span entire circumference/surface of the sphere).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5570 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5571 \textcolor{comment}{Finally,  MZ (minimum zone circle) stands somewhere between MC  and  MI in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5572 \textcolor{comment}{stability. It is somewhat regularized by "{}circumscribed"{} term of the merit}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5573 \textcolor{comment}{function; however, solutions to  MZ may be non-\/unique, and in some unlucky}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5574 \textcolor{comment}{cases it is also possible to "{}run away to infinity"{}.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5575 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5576 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5577 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: ON THE NONLINEARLY CONSTRAINED PROGRAMMING APPROACH}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5578 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5579 \textcolor{comment}{The problem formulation for MC  (minimum circumscribed   circle;  for  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5580 \textcolor{comment}{sake of simplicity we omit MZ and MI here) is:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5581 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5582 \textcolor{comment}{        [     [         ]2 ]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5583 \textcolor{comment}{    min [ max [ XY[i]-\/C ]  ]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5584 \textcolor{comment}{     C  [  i  [         ]  ]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5585 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5586 \textcolor{comment}{i.e. it is unconstrained nonsmooth optimization problem of finding  "{}best"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5587 \textcolor{comment}{central point, with radius R being unambiguously  determined  from  C.  In}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5588 \textcolor{comment}{order to move away from non-\/smoothness we use following reformulation:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5589 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5590 \textcolor{comment}{        [   ]                  [         ]2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5591 \textcolor{comment}{    min [ R ] subject to R>=0, [ XY[i]-\/C ]  <= R\string^2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5592 \textcolor{comment}{    C,R [   ]                  [         ]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5593 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5594 \textcolor{comment}{i.e. it becomes smooth quadratically constrained optimization problem with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5595 \textcolor{comment}{linear target function. Such problem statement is 100\% equivalent  to  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5596 \textcolor{comment}{original nonsmooth one, but much easier  to  approach.  We solve  it  with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5597 \textcolor{comment}{MinNLC solver provided by ALGLIB.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5598 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5599 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5600 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: ON INSTABILITY OF SEQUENTIAL LINEARIZATION APPROACH}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5601 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5602 \textcolor{comment}{ALGLIB  has  nonlinearly  constrained  solver which proved to be stable on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5603 \textcolor{comment}{such problems. However, some authors proposed to linearize constraints  in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5604 \textcolor{comment}{the vicinity of current approximation (Ci,Ri) and to get next  approximate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5605 \textcolor{comment}{solution (Ci+1,Ri+1) as solution to linear programming problem. Obviously,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5606 \textcolor{comment}{LP problems are easier than nonlinearly constrained ones.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5607 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5608 \textcolor{comment}{Indeed,  such approach  to   MC/MI/MZ   resulted   in  \string~10-\/20x increase in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5609 \textcolor{comment}{performance (when compared with NLC solver). However, it turned  out  that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5610 \textcolor{comment}{in some cases linearized model fails to predict correct direction for next}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5611 \textcolor{comment}{step and tells us that we converged to solution even when we are still 2-\/4}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5612 \textcolor{comment}{digits of precision away from it.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5613 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5614 \textcolor{comment}{It is important that it is not failure of LP solver -\/ it is failure of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5615 \textcolor{comment}{linear model;  even  when  solved  exactly,  it  fails  to  handle  subtle}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5616 \textcolor{comment}{nonlinearities which arise near the solution. We validated it by comparing}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5617 \textcolor{comment}{results returned by ALGLIB linear solver with that of MATLAB.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5618 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5619 \textcolor{comment}{In our experiments with linearization:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5620 \textcolor{comment}{* MC failed most often, at both realistic and synthetic datasets}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5621 \textcolor{comment}{* MI sometimes failed, but sometimes succeeded}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5622 \textcolor{comment}{* MZ often  succeeded; our guess is that presence of two independent  sets}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5623 \textcolor{comment}{  of constraints (one set for Rlo and another one for Rhi) and  two  terms}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5624 \textcolor{comment}{  in the target function (Rlo and Rhi) regularizes task,  so  when  linear}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5625 \textcolor{comment}{  model fails to handle nonlinearities from Rlo, it uses  Rhi  as  a  hint}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5626 \textcolor{comment}{  (and vice versa).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5627 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5628 \textcolor{comment}{Because linearization approach failed to achieve stable results, we do not}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5629 \textcolor{comment}{include it in ALGLIB.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5630 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5631 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5632 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5633 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 14.04.2017 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5634 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5635 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} fitspherex(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&xy, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t npoints, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nx, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t problemtype, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} epsx, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t aulits, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} penalty, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&cx, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&rlo, \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} \&rhi, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{5636 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#endif}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5637 }
\DoxyCodeLine{5638 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#if defined(AE\_COMPILE\_PARAMETRIC) || !defined(AE\_PARTIAL\_BUILD)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5639 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5640 \textcolor{comment}{This function  builds  non-\/periodic 2-\/dimensional parametric spline  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5641 \textcolor{comment}{starts at (X[0],Y[0]) and ends at (X[N-\/1],Y[N-\/1]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5642 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5643 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5644 \textcolor{comment}{    XY  -\/   points, array[0..N-\/1,0..1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5645 \textcolor{comment}{            XY[I,0:1] corresponds to the Ith point.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5646 \textcolor{comment}{            Order of points is important!}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5647 \textcolor{comment}{    N   -\/   points count, N>=5 for Akima splines, N>=2 for other types  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5648 \textcolor{comment}{            splines.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5649 \textcolor{comment}{    ST  -\/   spline type:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5650 \textcolor{comment}{            * 0     Akima spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5651 \textcolor{comment}{            * 1     parabolically terminated Catmull-\/Rom spline (Tension=0)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5652 \textcolor{comment}{            * 2     parabolically terminated cubic spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5653 \textcolor{comment}{    PT  -\/   parameterization type:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5654 \textcolor{comment}{            * 0     uniform}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5655 \textcolor{comment}{            * 1     chord length}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5656 \textcolor{comment}{            * 2     centripetal}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5657 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5658 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5659 \textcolor{comment}{    P   -\/   parametric spline interpolant}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5660 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5661 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5662 \textcolor{comment}{NOTES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5663 \textcolor{comment}{* this function  assumes  that  there all consequent points  are distinct.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5664 \textcolor{comment}{  I.e. (x0,y0)<>(x1,y1),  (x1,y1)<>(x2,y2),  (x2,y2)<>(x3,y3)  and  so on.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{5687 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5688 \textcolor{comment}{This  function  builds  periodic  2-\/dimensional  parametric  spline  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5689 \textcolor{comment}{starts at (X[0],Y[0]), goes through all points to (X[N-\/1],Y[N-\/1]) and then}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5690 \textcolor{comment}{back to (X[0],Y[0]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5691 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5692 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5693 \textcolor{comment}{    XY  -\/   points, array[0..N-\/1,0..1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5694 \textcolor{comment}{            XY[I,0:1] corresponds to the Ith point.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5695 \textcolor{comment}{            XY[N-\/1,0:1] must be different from XY[0,0:1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5696 \textcolor{comment}{            Order of points is important!}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5697 \textcolor{comment}{    N   -\/   points count, N>=3 for other types of splines.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5698 \textcolor{comment}{    ST  -\/   spline type:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5699 \textcolor{comment}{            * 1     Catmull-\/Rom spline (Tension=0) with cyclic boundary conditions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5700 \textcolor{comment}{            * 2     cubic spline with cyclic boundary conditions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5701 \textcolor{comment}{    PT  -\/   parameterization type:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5702 \textcolor{comment}{            * 0     uniform}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5703 \textcolor{comment}{            * 1     chord length}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5704 \textcolor{comment}{            * 2     centripetal}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5705 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5706 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5707 \textcolor{comment}{    P   -\/   parametric spline interpolant}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5708 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5709 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5710 \textcolor{comment}{NOTES:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5711 \textcolor{comment}{* this function  assumes  that there all consequent points  are  distinct.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5712 \textcolor{comment}{  I.e. (x0,y0)<>(x1,y1), (x1,y1)<>(x2,y2),  (x2,y2)<>(x3,y3)  and  so  on.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5713 \textcolor{comment}{  However, non-\/consequent points may coincide, i.e. we can  have  (x0,y0)=}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5714 \textcolor{comment}{  =(x2,y2).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5715 \textcolor{comment}{* last point of sequence is NOT equal to the first  point.  You  shouldn't}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5716 \textcolor{comment}{  make curve "{}explicitly periodic"{} by making them equal.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5717 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5718 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5719 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 28.05.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5720 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{5910 \textcolor{comment}{            * T in [0,1] corresponds to interval spanned by points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5911 \textcolor{comment}{            * for non-\/periodic splines T<0 (or T>1) correspond to parts of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{5912 \textcolor{comment}{              the curve before the first (after the last) point}}

\DoxyCodeLine{6027 }
\DoxyCodeLine{6028 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6029 \textcolor{comment}{This  subroutine fits piecewise linear curve to points with Ramer-\/Douglas-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6030 \textcolor{comment}{Peucker algorithm. This  function  performs PARAMETRIC fit, i.e. it can be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6031 \textcolor{comment}{used to fit curves like circles.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6032 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6033 \textcolor{comment}{On  input  it  accepts dataset which describes parametric multidimensional}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6034 \textcolor{comment}{curve X(t), with X being vector, and t taking values in [0,N), where N  is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6035 \textcolor{comment}{a number of points in dataset. As result, it returns reduced  dataset  X2,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6036 \textcolor{comment}{which can be used to build  parametric  curve  X2(t),  which  approximates}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6037 \textcolor{comment}{X(t) with desired precision (or has specified number of sections).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6038 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6039 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6040 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6041 \textcolor{comment}{    X       -\/   array of multidimensional points:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6042 \textcolor{comment}{                * at least N elements, leading N elements are used if more}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6043 \textcolor{comment}{                  than N elements were specified}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6044 \textcolor{comment}{                * order of points is IMPORTANT because  it  is  parametric}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6045 \textcolor{comment}{                  fit}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6046 \textcolor{comment}{                * each row of array is one point which has D coordinates}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6047 \textcolor{comment}{    N       -\/   number of elements in X}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6048 \textcolor{comment}{    D       -\/   number of dimensions (elements per row of X)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6049 \textcolor{comment}{    StopM   -\/   stopping condition -\/ desired number of sections:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6050 \textcolor{comment}{                * at most M sections are generated by this function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6051 \textcolor{comment}{                * less than M sections can be generated if we have N<M}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6052 \textcolor{comment}{                  (or some X are non-\/distinct).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6053 \textcolor{comment}{                * zero StopM means that algorithm does not stop after}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6054 \textcolor{comment}{                  achieving some pre-\/specified section count}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6055 \textcolor{comment}{    StopEps -\/   stopping condition -\/ desired precision:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6056 \textcolor{comment}{                * algorithm stops after error in each section is at most Eps}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6057 \textcolor{comment}{                * zero Eps means that algorithm does not stop after}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6058 \textcolor{comment}{                  achieving some pre-\/specified precision}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6059 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6060 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6061 \textcolor{comment}{    X2      -\/   array of corner points for piecewise approximation,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6062 \textcolor{comment}{                has length NSections+1 or zero (for NSections=0).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6063 \textcolor{comment}{    Idx2    -\/   array of indexes (parameter values):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6064 \textcolor{comment}{                * has length NSections+1 or zero (for NSections=0).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6065 \textcolor{comment}{                * each element of Idx2 corresponds to same-\/numbered}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6066 \textcolor{comment}{                  element of X2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6067 \textcolor{comment}{                * each element of Idx2 is index of  corresponding  element}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6068 \textcolor{comment}{                  of X2 at original array X, i.e. I-\/th  row  of  X2  is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6069 \textcolor{comment}{                  Idx2[I]-\/th row of X.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6070 \textcolor{comment}{                * elements of Idx2 can be treated as parameter values}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6071 \textcolor{comment}{                  which should be used when building new parametric curve}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6072 \textcolor{comment}{                * Idx2[0]=0, Idx2[NSections]=N-\/1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6073 \textcolor{comment}{    NSections-\/  number of sections found by algorithm, NSections<=M,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6074 \textcolor{comment}{                NSections can be zero for degenerate datasets}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6075 \textcolor{comment}{                (N<=1 or all X[] are non-\/distinct).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6076 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6077 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: algorithm stops after:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6078 \textcolor{comment}{      a) dividing curve into StopM sections}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6079 \textcolor{comment}{      b) achieving required precision StopEps}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6080 \textcolor{comment}{      c) dividing curve into N-\/1 sections}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6081 \textcolor{comment}{      If both StopM and StopEps are non-\/zero, algorithm is stopped by  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6082 \textcolor{comment}{      FIRST criterion which is satisfied. In case both StopM  and  StopEps}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6083 \textcolor{comment}{      are zero, algorithm stops because of (c).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6084 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6085 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6086 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 02.10.2014 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6087 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6088 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} parametricrdpfixed(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t d, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t stopm, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} stopeps, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&x2, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1integer__1d__array}{integer\_1d\_array}} \&idx2, ae\_int\_t \&nsections, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{6099 \textcolor{comment}{Important properties of s\_out:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6100 \textcolor{comment}{* it contains alphanumeric characters, dots, underscores, minus signs}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6101 \textcolor{comment}{* these symbols are grouped into words, which are separated by spaces}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6102 \textcolor{comment}{  and Windows-\/style (CR+LF) newlines}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6103 \textcolor{comment}{* although  serializer  uses  spaces and CR+LF as separators, you can }}
\DoxyCodeLine{6104 \textcolor{comment}{  replace any separator character by arbitrary combination of spaces,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6105 \textcolor{comment}{  tabs, Windows or Unix newlines. It allows flexible reformatting  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6106 \textcolor{comment}{  the  string  in  case you want to include it into text or XML file. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{6107 \textcolor{comment}{  But you should not insert separators into the middle of the "{}words"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6108 \textcolor{comment}{  nor you should change case of letters.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6109 \textcolor{comment}{* s\_out can be freely moved between 32-\/bit and 64-\/bit systems, little}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6110 \textcolor{comment}{  and big endian machines, and so on. You can serialize structure  on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6111 \textcolor{comment}{  32-\/bit machine and unserialize it on 64-\/bit one (or vice versa), or}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6112 \textcolor{comment}{  serialize  it  on  SPARC  and  unserialize  on  x86.  You  can also }}
\DoxyCodeLine{6113 \textcolor{comment}{  serialize  it  in  C++ version of ALGLIB and unserialize in C\# one, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{6114 \textcolor{comment}{  and vice versa.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6115 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{6166 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine calculates the value of the bilinear or bicubic spline  at}}

\DoxyCodeLine{6168 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6169 \textcolor{comment}{Input parameters:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6170 \textcolor{comment}{    C   -\/   spline interpolant.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{6172 \textcolor{comment}{}}

\DoxyCodeLine{6406 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6407 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine unpacks two-\/dimensional spline into the coefficients table}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6408 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6409 \textcolor{comment}{Input parameters:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6410 \textcolor{comment}{    C   -\/   spline interpolant.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6411 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6412 \textcolor{comment}{Result:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6413 \textcolor{comment}{    M, N-\/   grid size (x-\/axis and y-\/axis)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6414 \textcolor{comment}{    D   -\/   number of components}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6415 \textcolor{comment}{    Tbl -\/   coefficients table, unpacked format,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6416 \textcolor{comment}{            D -\/ components: [0..(N-\/1)*(M-\/1)*D-\/1, 0..19].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6417 \textcolor{comment}{            For T=0..D-\/1 (component index), I = 0...N-\/2 (x index),}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6418 \textcolor{comment}{            J=0..M-\/2 (y index):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6419 \textcolor{comment}{                K :=  T + I*D + J*D*(N-\/1)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6420 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6421 \textcolor{comment}{                K-\/th row stores decomposition for T-\/th component of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6422 \textcolor{comment}{                vector-\/valued function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6423 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6424 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,0] = X[i]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6425 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,1] = X[i+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6426 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,2] = Y[j]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6427 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,3] = Y[j+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6428 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,4] = C00}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6429 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,5] = C01}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6430 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,6] = C02}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6431 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,7] = C03}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6432 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,8] = C10}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6433 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,9] = C11}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6434 \textcolor{comment}{                ...}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6435 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[K,19] = C33}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6436 \textcolor{comment}{            On each grid square spline is equals to:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6437 \textcolor{comment}{                S(x) = SUM(c[i,j]*(t\string^i)*(u\string^j), i=0..3, j=0..3)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6438 \textcolor{comment}{                t = x-\/x[j]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6439 \textcolor{comment}{                u = y-\/y[i]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6440 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6441 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6442 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 16.04.2012 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6443 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6444 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline2dunpackv(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline2dinterpolant}{spline2dinterpolant}} \&c, ae\_int\_t \&m, ae\_int\_t \&n, ae\_int\_t \&d, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&tbl, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{6482 }
\DoxyCodeLine{6483 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6484 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine creates least squares solver used to  fit  2D  splines  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6485 \textcolor{comment}{irregularly sampled (scattered) data.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6486 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6487 \textcolor{comment}{Solver object is used to perform spline fits as follows:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6488 \textcolor{comment}{* solver object is created with spline2dbuildercreate() function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6489 \textcolor{comment}{* dataset is added with spline2dbuildersetpoints() function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6490 \textcolor{comment}{* fit area is chosen:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6491 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetarea()     -\/ for user-\/defined area}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6492 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetareaauto() -\/ for automatically chosen area}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6493 \textcolor{comment}{* number of grid nodes is chosen with spline2dbuildersetgrid()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6494 \textcolor{comment}{* prior term is chosen with one of the following functions:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6495 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetlinterm()   to set linear prior}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6496 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetconstterm() to set constant prior}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6497 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetzeroterm()  to set zero prior}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6498 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetuserterm()  to set user-\/defined constant prior}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6499 \textcolor{comment}{* solver algorithm is chosen with either:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6500 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetalgoblocklls() -\/ BlockLLS algorithm, medium-\/scale problems}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6501 \textcolor{comment}{  * spline2dbuildersetalgofastddm()  -\/ FastDDM algorithm, large-\/scale problems}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6502 \textcolor{comment}{* finally, fitting itself is performed with spline2dfit() function.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6503 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6504 \textcolor{comment}{Most of the steps above can be omitted,  solver  is  configured with  good}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6505 \textcolor{comment}{defaults. The minimum is to call:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6506 \textcolor{comment}{* spline2dbuildercreate() to create solver object}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6507 \textcolor{comment}{* spline2dbuildersetpoints() to specify dataset}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6508 \textcolor{comment}{* spline2dbuildersetgrid() to tell how many nodes you need}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6509 \textcolor{comment}{* spline2dfit() to perform fit}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6510 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6511 \textcolor{comment}{  ! COMMERCIAL EDITION OF ALGLIB:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6512 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6513 \textcolor{comment}{  ! Commercial Edition of ALGLIB includes following important improvements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6514 \textcolor{comment}{  ! of this function:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6515 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * high-\/performance native backend with same C\# interface (C\# version)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6516 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * multithreading support (C++ and C\# versions)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6517 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * hardware vendor (Intel) implementations of linear algebra primitives}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6518 \textcolor{comment}{  !   (C++ and C\# versions, x86/x64 platform)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6519 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6520 \textcolor{comment}{  ! We recommend you to read 'Working with commercial version' section  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6521 \textcolor{comment}{  ! ALGLIB Reference Manual in order to find out how to  use  performance-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6522 \textcolor{comment}{  ! related features provided by commercial edition of ALGLIB.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6523 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6524 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6525 \textcolor{comment}{    D   -\/   positive number, number of Y-\/components: D=1 for simple scalar}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6526 \textcolor{comment}{            fit, D>1 for vector-\/valued spline fitting.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6527 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6528 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6529 \textcolor{comment}{    S   -\/   solver object}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6530 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6531 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6532 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 29.01.2018 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6533 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6534 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline2dbuildercreate(\textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t d, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline2dbuilder}{spline2dbuilder}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{6535 }

\DoxyCodeLine{6649 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6650 \textcolor{comment}{This  function  sets  nodes  count  for  2D spline interpolant. Fitting is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6651 \textcolor{comment}{performed on area defined with one of the "{}setarea"{}  functions;  this  one}}

\DoxyCodeLine{6658 \textcolor{comment}{                created at the boundaries.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6659 \textcolor{comment}{    KY      -\/   nodes count for the first (Y) dimension; fitting  interval}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6660 \textcolor{comment}{                [YA,YB] is separated into KY-\/1 subintervals, with KY nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6661 \textcolor{comment}{                created at the boundaries.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6662 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6663 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: at  least  4  nodes  is  created in each dimension, so KX and KY are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6664 \textcolor{comment}{      silently increased if needed.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6665 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6666 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
