\DoxyCodeLine{6672 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6673 \textcolor{comment}{This  function  allows  you to choose least squares solver used to perform}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6674 \textcolor{comment}{fitting. This function sets solver algorithm to "{}FastDDM"{}, which  performs}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6675 \textcolor{comment}{fast parallel fitting by splitting problem into smaller chunks and merging}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6676 \textcolor{comment}{results together.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6677 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6678 \textcolor{comment}{This solver is optimized for large-\/scale problems, starting  from  256x256}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6679 \textcolor{comment}{grids, and up to 10000x10000 grids. Of course, it will  work  for  smaller}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6680 \textcolor{comment}{grids too.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6681 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6682 \textcolor{comment}{More detailed description of the algorithm is given below:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6683 \textcolor{comment}{* algorithm generates hierarchy  of  nested  grids,  ranging  from  \string~16x16}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6684 \textcolor{comment}{  (topmost "{}layer"{} of the model) to \string~KX*KY one (final layer). Upper layers}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6685 \textcolor{comment}{  model global behavior of the function, lower layers are  used  to  model}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6686 \textcolor{comment}{  fine details. Moving from layer to layer doubles grid density.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6687 \textcolor{comment}{* fitting  is  started  from  topmost  layer, subsequent layers are fitted}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6688 \textcolor{comment}{  using residuals from previous ones.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6689 \textcolor{comment}{* user may choose to skip generation of upper layers and generate  only  a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6690 \textcolor{comment}{  few bottom ones, which  will  result  in  much  better  performance  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6691 \textcolor{comment}{  parallelization efficiency, at the cost of algorithm inability to "{}patch"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6692 \textcolor{comment}{  large holes in the dataset.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6693 \textcolor{comment}{* every layer is regularized using progressively increasing regularization}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6694 \textcolor{comment}{  coefficient; thus, increasing  LambdaV  penalizes  fine  details  first,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6695 \textcolor{comment}{  leaving lower frequencies almost intact for a while.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6696 \textcolor{comment}{* after fitting is done, all layers are merged together into  one  bicubic}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6697 \textcolor{comment}{  spline}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6698 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6699 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: regularization coefficient used by  this  solver  is  different}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6700 \textcolor{comment}{           from the one used by  BlockLLS.  Latter  utilizes  nonlinearity}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6701 \textcolor{comment}{           penalty,  which  is  global  in  nature  (large  regularization}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6702 \textcolor{comment}{           results in global linear trend being  extracted);  this  solver}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6703 \textcolor{comment}{           uses another, localized form of penalty, which is suitable  for}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6704 \textcolor{comment}{           parallel processing.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6705 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6706 \textcolor{comment}{Notes on memory and performance:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6707 \textcolor{comment}{* memory requirements: most memory is consumed  during  modeling   of  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6708 \textcolor{comment}{  higher layers; \string~[512*NPoints] bytes is required for a  model  with  full}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6709 \textcolor{comment}{  hierarchy of grids being generated. However, if you skip a  few  topmost}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6710 \textcolor{comment}{  layers, you will get nearly constant (wrt. points count and  grid  size)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6711 \textcolor{comment}{  memory consumption.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6712 \textcolor{comment}{* serial running time: O(K*K)+O(NPoints) for a KxK grid}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6713 \textcolor{comment}{* parallelism potential: good. You may get  nearly  linear  speed-\/up  when}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6714 \textcolor{comment}{  performing fitting with just a few layers. Adding more layers results in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6715 \textcolor{comment}{  model becoming more global, which somewhat  reduces  efficiency  of  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6716 \textcolor{comment}{  parallel code.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6717 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6718 \textcolor{comment}{  ! COMMERCIAL EDITION OF ALGLIB:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6719 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6720 \textcolor{comment}{  ! Commercial Edition of ALGLIB includes following important improvements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6721 \textcolor{comment}{  ! of this function:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6722 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * high-\/performance native backend with same C\# interface (C\# version)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6723 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * multithreading support (C++ and C\# versions)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6724 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * hardware vendor (Intel) implementations of linear algebra primitives}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6725 \textcolor{comment}{  !   (C++ and C\# versions, x86/x64 platform)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6726 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6727 \textcolor{comment}{  ! We recommend you to read 'Working with commercial version' section  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6728 \textcolor{comment}{  ! ALGLIB Reference Manual in order to find out how to  use  performance-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6729 \textcolor{comment}{  ! related features provided by commercial edition of ALGLIB.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6730 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6731 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6732 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   spline 2D builder object}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6733 \textcolor{comment}{    NLayers -\/   number of layers in the model:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6734 \textcolor{comment}{                * NLayers>=1 means that up  to  chosen  number  of  bottom}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6735 \textcolor{comment}{                  layers is fitted}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6736 \textcolor{comment}{                * NLayers=0 means that maximum number of layers is  chosen}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6737 \textcolor{comment}{                  (according to current grid size)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6738 \textcolor{comment}{                * NLayers<=-\/1 means that up to |NLayers| topmost layers is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6739 \textcolor{comment}{                  skipped}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6740 \textcolor{comment}{                Recommendations:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6741 \textcolor{comment}{                * good "{}default"{} value is 2 layers}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6742 \textcolor{comment}{                * you may need  more  layers,  if  your  dataset  is  very}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6743 \textcolor{comment}{                  irregular and you want to "{}patch"{}  large  holes.  For  a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6744 \textcolor{comment}{                  grid step H (equal to AreaWidth/GridSize) you may expect}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6745 \textcolor{comment}{                  that last layer reproduces variations at distance H (and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6746 \textcolor{comment}{                  can patch holes that wide); that higher  layers  operate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6747 \textcolor{comment}{                  at distances 2*H, 4*H, 8*H and so on.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6748 \textcolor{comment}{                * good value for "{}bullletproof"{} mode is  NLayers=0,  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6749 \textcolor{comment}{                  results in complete hierarchy of layers being generated.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6750 \textcolor{comment}{    LambdaV -\/   regularization coefficient, chosen in such a way  that  it}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6751 \textcolor{comment}{                penalizes bottom layers (fine details) first.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6752 \textcolor{comment}{                LambdaV>=0, zero value means that no penalty is applied.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6753 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6754 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6755 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 05.02.2018 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6756 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6757 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline2dbuildersetalgofastddm(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline2dbuilder}{spline2dbuilder}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nlayers, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} lambdav, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{6758 }
\DoxyCodeLine{6759 }
\DoxyCodeLine{6760 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6761 \textcolor{comment}{This  function  allows  you to choose least squares solver used to perform}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6762 \textcolor{comment}{fitting. This function sets solver algorithm to "{}BlockLLS"{}, which performs}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6763 \textcolor{comment}{least squares fitting  with  fast  sparse  direct  solver,  with  optional}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6764 \textcolor{comment}{nonsmoothness penalty being applied.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6765 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6766 \textcolor{comment}{Nonlinearity penalty has the following form:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6767 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6768 \textcolor{comment}{                          [                                            ]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6769 \textcolor{comment}{    P() \string~ Lambda* integral[ (d2S/dx2)\string^2 + 2*(d2S/dxdy)\string^2 + (d2S/dy2)\string^2 ]dxdy}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6770 \textcolor{comment}{                          [                                            ]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6771 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6772 \textcolor{comment}{here integral is calculated over entire grid, and "{}\string~"{} means "{}proportional"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6773 \textcolor{comment}{because integral is normalized after calcilation. Extremely  large  values}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6774 \textcolor{comment}{of Lambda result in linear fit being performed.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6775 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6776 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: this algorithm is the most robust and controllable one,  but  it  is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6777 \textcolor{comment}{      limited by 512x512 grids and (say) up to 1.000.000 points.  However,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6778 \textcolor{comment}{      ALGLIB has one more  spline  solver:  FastDDM  algorithm,  which  is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6779 \textcolor{comment}{      intended for really large-\/scale problems (in 10M-\/100M range). FastDDM}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6780 \textcolor{comment}{      algorithm also has better parallelism properties.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6781 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6782 \textcolor{comment}{More information on BlockLLS solver:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6783 \textcolor{comment}{* memory requirements: \string~[32*K\string^3+256*NPoints]  bytes  for  KxK  grid   with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6784 \textcolor{comment}{  NPoints-\/sized dataset}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6785 \textcolor{comment}{* serial running time: O(K\string^4+NPoints)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6786 \textcolor{comment}{* parallelism potential: limited. You may get some sublinear gain when}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6787 \textcolor{comment}{  working with large grids (K's in 256..512 range)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6788 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6789 \textcolor{comment}{  ! COMMERCIAL EDITION OF ALGLIB:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6790 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6791 \textcolor{comment}{  ! Commercial Edition of ALGLIB includes following important improvements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6792 \textcolor{comment}{  ! of this function:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6793 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * high-\/performance native backend with same C\# interface (C\# version)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6794 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * multithreading support (C++ and C\# versions)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6795 \textcolor{comment}{  ! * hardware vendor (Intel) implementations of linear algebra primitives}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6796 \textcolor{comment}{  !   (C++ and C\# versions, x86/x64 platform)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6797 \textcolor{comment}{  !}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6798 \textcolor{comment}{  ! We recommend you to read 'Working with commercial version' section  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6799 \textcolor{comment}{  ! ALGLIB Reference Manual in order to find out how to  use  performance-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6800 \textcolor{comment}{  ! related features provided by commercial edition of ALGLIB.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6801 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6802 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6803 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   spline 2D builder object}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6804 \textcolor{comment}{    LambdaNS-\/   non-\/negative value:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6805 \textcolor{comment}{                * positive value means that some smoothing is applied}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6806 \textcolor{comment}{                * zero value means  that  no  smoothing  is  applied,  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6807 \textcolor{comment}{                  corresponding entries of design matrix  are  numerically}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6808 \textcolor{comment}{                  zero and dropped from consideration.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6809 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6810 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6811 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 05.02.2018 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6812 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6813 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline2dbuildersetalgoblocklls(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline2dbuilder}{spline2dbuilder}} \&state, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} lambdans, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{6934 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6935 \textcolor{comment}{Trilinear spline resampling}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6936 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6937 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6938 \textcolor{comment}{    A           -\/   array[0..OldXCount*OldYCount*OldZCount-\/1], function}}

\DoxyCodeLine{6973 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine builds trilinear vector-\/valued spline.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6974 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6975 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6976 \textcolor{comment}{    X   -\/   spline abscissas,  array[0..N-\/1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6977 \textcolor{comment}{    Y   -\/   spline ordinates,  array[0..M-\/1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6978 \textcolor{comment}{    Z   -\/   spline applicates, array[0..L-\/1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6979 \textcolor{comment}{    F   -\/   function values, array[0..M*N*L*D-\/1]:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6980 \textcolor{comment}{            * first D elements store D values at (X[0],Y[0],Z[0])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6981 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[1],Y[0],Z[0])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6982 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[2],Y[0],Z[0])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6983 \textcolor{comment}{            * ...}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6984 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[0],Y[1],Z[0])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6985 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[1],Y[1],Z[0])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6986 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[2],Y[1],Z[0])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6987 \textcolor{comment}{            * ...}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6988 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[0],Y[0],Z[1])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6989 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[1],Y[0],Z[1])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6990 \textcolor{comment}{            * next D elements store D values at (X[2],Y[0],Z[1])}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6991 \textcolor{comment}{            * ...}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6992 \textcolor{comment}{            * general form -\/ D function values at (X[i],Y[j]) are stored}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6993 \textcolor{comment}{              at F[D*(N*(M*K+J)+I)...D*(N*(M*K+J)+I)+D-\/1].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6994 \textcolor{comment}{    M,N,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6995 \textcolor{comment}{    L   -\/   grid size, M>=2, N>=2, L>=2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6996 \textcolor{comment}{    D   -\/   vector dimension, D>=1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6997 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6998 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{6999 \textcolor{comment}{    C   -\/   spline interpolant}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7000 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7001 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7002 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 26.04.2012 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7003 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{7050 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7051 \textcolor{comment}{This subroutine unpacks tri-\/dimensional spline into the coefficients table}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7052 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7053 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7054 \textcolor{comment}{    C   -\/   spline interpolant.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7055 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7056 \textcolor{comment}{Result:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7057 \textcolor{comment}{    N   -\/   grid size (X)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7058 \textcolor{comment}{    M   -\/   grid size (Y)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7059 \textcolor{comment}{    L   -\/   grid size (Z)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7060 \textcolor{comment}{    D   -\/   number of components}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7061 \textcolor{comment}{    SType-\/  spline type. Currently, only one spline type is supported:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7062 \textcolor{comment}{            trilinear spline, as indicated by SType=1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7063 \textcolor{comment}{    Tbl -\/   spline coefficients: [0..(N-\/1)*(M-\/1)*(L-\/1)*D-\/1, 0..13].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7064 \textcolor{comment}{            For T=0..D-\/1 (component index), I = 0...N-\/2 (x index),}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7065 \textcolor{comment}{            J=0..M-\/2 (y index), K=0..L-\/2 (z index):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7066 \textcolor{comment}{                Q := T + I*D + J*D*(N-\/1) + K*D*(N-\/1)*(M-\/1),}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7067 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7068 \textcolor{comment}{                Q-\/th row stores decomposition for T-\/th component of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7069 \textcolor{comment}{                vector-\/valued function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7070 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7071 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,0] = X[i]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7072 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,1] = X[i+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7073 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,2] = Y[j]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7074 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,3] = Y[j+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7075 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,4] = Z[k]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7076 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,5] = Z[k+1]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7077 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7078 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,6] = C000}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7079 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,7] = C100}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7080 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,8] = C010}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7081 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,9] = C110}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7082 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,10]= C001}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7083 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,11]= C101}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7084 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,12]= C011}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7085 \textcolor{comment}{                Tbl[Q,13]= C111}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7086 \textcolor{comment}{            On each grid square spline is equals to:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7087 \textcolor{comment}{                S(x) = SUM(c[i,j,k]*(x\string^i)*(y\string^j)*(z\string^k), i=0..1, j=0..1, k=0..1)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7088 \textcolor{comment}{                t = x-\/x[j]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7089 \textcolor{comment}{                u = y-\/y[i]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7090 \textcolor{comment}{                v = z-\/z[k]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7091 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7092 \textcolor{comment}{            NOTE: format of Tbl is given for SType=1. Future versions of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7093 \textcolor{comment}{                  ALGLIB can use different formats for different values of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7094 \textcolor{comment}{                  SType.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7095 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7096 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7097 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 26.04.2012 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7098 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{7164 \textcolor{comment}{It was superseded by spline1dfit(), which is an orders of magnitude faster}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7165 \textcolor{comment}{and more memory-\/efficient implementation.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7166 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7167 \textcolor{comment}{Do NOT use this function in the new code!}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7168 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7169 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB PROJECT -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7170 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 19.10.2010 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7171 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7172 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} spline1dfitpenalizedw(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&x, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&y, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&w, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t m, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} rho, ae\_int\_t \&info, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dinterpolant}{spline1dinterpolant}} \&s, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1spline1dfitreport}{spline1dfitreport}} \&rep, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{7176 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#if defined(AE\_COMPILE\_RBF) || !defined(AE\_PARTIAL\_BUILD)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7177 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7178 \textcolor{comment}{This function serializes data structure to string.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7179 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7180 \textcolor{comment}{Important properties of s\_out:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7181 \textcolor{comment}{* it contains alphanumeric characters, dots, underscores, minus signs}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7182 \textcolor{comment}{* these symbols are grouped into words, which are separated by spaces}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7183 \textcolor{comment}{  and Windows-\/style (CR+LF) newlines}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7184 \textcolor{comment}{* although  serializer  uses  spaces and CR+LF as separators, you can }}
\DoxyCodeLine{7185 \textcolor{comment}{  replace any separator character by arbitrary combination of spaces,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7186 \textcolor{comment}{  tabs, Windows or Unix newlines. It allows flexible reformatting  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7187 \textcolor{comment}{  the  string  in  case you want to include it into text or XML file. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{7188 \textcolor{comment}{  But you should not insert separators into the middle of the "{}words"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7189 \textcolor{comment}{  nor you should change case of letters.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7190 \textcolor{comment}{* s\_out can be freely moved between 32-\/bit and 64-\/bit systems, little}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7191 \textcolor{comment}{  and big endian machines, and so on. You can serialize structure  on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7192 \textcolor{comment}{  32-\/bit machine and unserialize it on 64-\/bit one (or vice versa), or}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7193 \textcolor{comment}{  serialize  it  on  SPARC  and  unserialize  on  x86.  You  can also }}
\DoxyCodeLine{7194 \textcolor{comment}{  serialize  it  in  C++ version of ALGLIB and unserialize in C\# one, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{7195 \textcolor{comment}{  and vice versa.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7196 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7197 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfserialize(\mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&obj, std::string \&s\_out);}

\DoxyCodeLine{7226 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7227 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7228 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7229 \textcolor{comment}{This function creates RBF  model  for  a  scalar (NY=1)  or  vector (NY>1)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7230 \textcolor{comment}{function in a NX-\/dimensional space (NX>=1).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7231 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7232 \textcolor{comment}{Newly created model is empty. It can be used for interpolation right after}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7233 \textcolor{comment}{creation, but it just returns zeros. You have to add points to the  model,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7234 \textcolor{comment}{tune interpolation settings, and then  call  model  construction  function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7235 \textcolor{comment}{rbfbuildmodel() which will update model according to your specification.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7236 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7237 \textcolor{comment}{USAGE:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7238 \textcolor{comment}{1. User creates model with rbfcreate()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7239 \textcolor{comment}{2. User adds dataset with rbfsetpoints() (points do NOT have to  be  on  a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7240 \textcolor{comment}{   regular grid) or rbfsetpointsandscales().}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7241 \textcolor{comment}{3. (OPTIONAL) User chooses polynomial term by calling:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7242 \textcolor{comment}{   * rbflinterm() to set linear term}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7243 \textcolor{comment}{   * rbfconstterm() to set constant term}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7244 \textcolor{comment}{   * rbfzeroterm() to set zero term}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7245 \textcolor{comment}{   By default, linear term is used.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7246 \textcolor{comment}{4. User tweaks algorithm properties with  rbfsetalgohierarchical()  method}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7247 \textcolor{comment}{   (or chooses one of the legacy algorithms -\/ QNN  (rbfsetalgoqnn)  or  ML}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7248 \textcolor{comment}{   (rbfsetalgomultilayer)).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7249 \textcolor{comment}{5. User calls rbfbuildmodel() function which rebuilds model  according  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7250 \textcolor{comment}{   the specification}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7251 \textcolor{comment}{6. User may call rbfcalc() to calculate model value at the specified point,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7252 \textcolor{comment}{   rbfgridcalc() to  calculate   model  values at the points of the regular}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7253 \textcolor{comment}{   grid. User may extract model coefficients with rbfunpack() call.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7254 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7255 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: we recommend you to use latest model construction  algorithm  -\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7256 \textcolor{comment}{           hierarchical RBFs, which is activated by rbfsetalgohierarchical()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7257 \textcolor{comment}{           function. This algorithm is the fastest one, and  most  memory-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7258 \textcolor{comment}{           efficient.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7259 \textcolor{comment}{           However,  it  is  incompatible  with older versions  of  ALGLIB}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7260 \textcolor{comment}{           (pre-\/3.11). So, if you serialize hierarchical model,  you  will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7261 \textcolor{comment}{           be unable to load it in pre-\/3.11 ALGLIB. Other model types (QNN}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7262 \textcolor{comment}{           and RBF-\/ML) are still backward-\/compatible.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7263 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7264 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7265 \textcolor{comment}{    NX      -\/   dimension of the space, NX>=1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7266 \textcolor{comment}{    NY      -\/   function dimension, NY>=1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7267 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7268 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7269 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model (initially equals to zero)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7270 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7271 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 1: memory requirements. RBF models require amount of memory  which is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7272 \textcolor{comment}{        proportional  to the number of data points. Some additional memory}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7273 \textcolor{comment}{        is allocated during model construction, but most of this memory is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7274 \textcolor{comment}{        freed after model coefficients  are  calculated.  Amount  of  this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7275 \textcolor{comment}{        additional memory depends on model  construction  algorithm  being}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7276 \textcolor{comment}{        used.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7277 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7278 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE 2: prior to ALGLIB version 3.11, RBF models supported  only  NX=2  or}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7279 \textcolor{comment}{        NX=3. Any  attempt  to  create  single-\/dimensional  or  more  than}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7280 \textcolor{comment}{        3-\/dimensional RBF model resulted in exception.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7281 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7282 \textcolor{comment}{        ALGLIB 3.11 supports any NX>0, but models created with  NX!=2  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7283 \textcolor{comment}{        NX!=3 are incompatible with (a) older versions of ALGLIB, (b)  old}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7284 \textcolor{comment}{        model construction algorithms (QNN or RBF-\/ML).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7285 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7286 \textcolor{comment}{        So, if you create a model with NX=2 or NX=3,  then,  depending  on}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7287 \textcolor{comment}{        specific  model construction algorithm being chosen, you will (QNN}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7288 \textcolor{comment}{        and RBF-\/ML) or will not (HierarchicalRBF) get backward compatibility}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7289 \textcolor{comment}{        with older versions of ALGLIB. You have a choice here.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7290 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7291 \textcolor{comment}{        However, if you create a model with NX neither 2 nor 3,  you  have}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7292 \textcolor{comment}{        no backward compatibility from the start, and you  are  forced  to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7293 \textcolor{comment}{        use hierarchical RBFs and ALGLIB 3.11 or later.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7294 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7295 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7296 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 13.12.2011, 20.06.2016 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7297 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7298 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfcreate(\textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nx, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t ny, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7299 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7300 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7301 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7302 \textcolor{comment}{This function creates buffer  structure  which  can  be  used  to  perform}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7303 \textcolor{comment}{parallel  RBF  model  evaluations  (with  one  RBF  model  instance  being}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7304 \textcolor{comment}{used from multiple threads, as long as  different  threads  use  different}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7305 \textcolor{comment}{instances of buffer).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7306 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7307 \textcolor{comment}{This buffer object can be used with  rbftscalcbuf()  function  (here  "{}ts"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7308 \textcolor{comment}{stands for "{}thread-\/safe"{}, "{}buf"{} is a suffix which denotes  function  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7309 \textcolor{comment}{reuses previously allocated output space).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7310 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7311 \textcolor{comment}{How to use it:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7312 \textcolor{comment}{* create RBF model structure with rbfcreate()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7313 \textcolor{comment}{* load data, tune parameters}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7314 \textcolor{comment}{* call rbfbuildmodel()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7315 \textcolor{comment}{* call rbfcreatecalcbuffer(), once per thread working with RBF model  (you}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7316 \textcolor{comment}{  should call this function only AFTER call to rbfbuildmodel(), see  below}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7317 \textcolor{comment}{  for more information)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7318 \textcolor{comment}{* call rbftscalcbuf() from different threads,  with  each  thread  working}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7319 \textcolor{comment}{  with its own copy of buffer object.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7320 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7321 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7322 \textcolor{comment}{    S           -\/   RBF model}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7323 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7324 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7325 \textcolor{comment}{    Buf         -\/   external buffer.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7326 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7327 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7328 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: buffer object should be used only with  RBF model object  which}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7329 \textcolor{comment}{           was used to initialize buffer. Any attempt to use buffer   with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7330 \textcolor{comment}{           different object is dangerous -\/ you may  get  memory  violation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7331 \textcolor{comment}{           error because sizes of internal arrays do not fit to dimensions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7332 \textcolor{comment}{           of RBF structure.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7333 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7334 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: you  should  call  this function only for model which was built}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7335 \textcolor{comment}{           with rbfbuildmodel() function, after successful  invocation  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7336 \textcolor{comment}{           rbfbuildmodel().  Sizes   of   some   internal  structures  are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7337 \textcolor{comment}{           determined only after model is built, so buffer object  created}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7338 \textcolor{comment}{           before model  construction  stage  will  be  useless  (and  any}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7339 \textcolor{comment}{           attempt to use it will result in exception).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7340 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7341 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7342 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 02.04.2016 by Sergey Bochkanov}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7343 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7344 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfcreatecalcbuffer(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfcalcbuffer}{rbfcalcbuffer}} \&buf, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7345 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7346 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7347 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7348 \textcolor{comment}{This function adds dataset.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7349 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7350 \textcolor{comment}{This function overrides results of the previous calls, i.e. multiple calls}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7351 \textcolor{comment}{of this function will result in only the last set being added.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7352 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7353 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: ALGLIB version 3.11 and later allows you to specify  a  set  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7354 \textcolor{comment}{           per-\/dimension scales. Interpolation radii are multiplied by the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7355 \textcolor{comment}{           scale vector. It may be useful if you have mixed spatio-\/temporal}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7356 \textcolor{comment}{           data (say, a set of 3D slices recorded at different times).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7357 \textcolor{comment}{           You should call rbfsetpointsandscales() function  to  use  this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7358 \textcolor{comment}{           feature.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7359 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7360 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7361 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model, initialized by rbfcreate() call.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7362 \textcolor{comment}{    XY      -\/   points, array[N,NX+NY]. One row corresponds to  one  point}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7363 \textcolor{comment}{                in the dataset. First NX elements  are  coordinates,  next}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7364 \textcolor{comment}{                NY elements are function values. Array may  be larger than}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7365 \textcolor{comment}{                specified, in  this  case  only leading [N,NX+NY] elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7366 \textcolor{comment}{                will be used.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7367 \textcolor{comment}{    N       -\/   number of points in the dataset}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7368 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7369 \textcolor{comment}{After you've added dataset and (optionally) tuned algorithm  settings  you}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7370 \textcolor{comment}{should call rbfbuildmodel() in order to build a model for you.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7371 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7372 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: dataset added by this function is not saved during model serialization.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7373 \textcolor{comment}{      MODEL ITSELF is serialized, but data used to build it are not.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7374 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7375 \textcolor{comment}{      So, if you 1) add dataset to  empty  RBF  model,  2)  serialize  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7376 \textcolor{comment}{      unserialize it, then you will get an empty RBF model with no dataset}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7377 \textcolor{comment}{      being attached.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7378 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7379 \textcolor{comment}{      From the other side, if you call rbfbuildmodel() between (1) and (2),}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7380 \textcolor{comment}{      then after (2) you will get your fully constructed RBF model  -\/  but}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7381 \textcolor{comment}{      again with no dataset attached, so subsequent calls to rbfbuildmodel()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7382 \textcolor{comment}{      will produce empty model.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7383 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7384 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7385 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7386 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 13.12.2011 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7387 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7388 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetpoints(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&xy, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7389 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetpoints(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&xy, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7390 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7391 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7392 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7393 \textcolor{comment}{This function adds dataset and a vector of per-\/dimension scales.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7394 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7395 \textcolor{comment}{It may be useful if you have mixed spatio-\/temporal data -\/ say, a set of 3D}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7396 \textcolor{comment}{slices recorded at different times. Such data typically require  different}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7397 \textcolor{comment}{RBF radii for spatial and temporal dimensions. ALGLIB solves this  problem}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7398 \textcolor{comment}{by specifying single RBF radius, which is (optionally) multiplied  by  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7399 \textcolor{comment}{scale vector.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7400 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7401 \textcolor{comment}{This function overrides results of the previous calls, i.e. multiple calls}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7402 \textcolor{comment}{of this function will result in only the last set being added.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7403 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7404 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: only HierarchicalRBF algorithm can work with scaled points. So,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7405 \textcolor{comment}{           using this function results in RBF models which can be used  in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7406 \textcolor{comment}{           ALGLIB 3.11 or later. Previous versions of the library will  be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7407 \textcolor{comment}{           unable  to unserialize models produced by HierarchicalRBF algo.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7408 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7409 \textcolor{comment}{           Any attempt to use this function with RBF-\/ML or QNN  algorithms}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7410 \textcolor{comment}{           will result  in  -\/3  error  code   being   returned  (incorrect}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7411 \textcolor{comment}{           algorithm).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7412 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7413 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7414 \textcolor{comment}{    R       -\/   RBF model, initialized by rbfcreate() call.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7415 \textcolor{comment}{    XY      -\/   points, array[N,NX+NY]. One row corresponds to  one  point}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7416 \textcolor{comment}{                in the dataset. First NX elements  are  coordinates,  next}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7417 \textcolor{comment}{                NY elements are function values. Array may  be larger than}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7418 \textcolor{comment}{                specified, in  this  case  only leading [N,NX+NY] elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7419 \textcolor{comment}{                will be used.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7420 \textcolor{comment}{    N       -\/   number of points in the dataset}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7421 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   array[NX], scale vector, S[i]>0.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7422 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7423 \textcolor{comment}{After you've added dataset and (optionally) tuned algorithm  settings  you}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7424 \textcolor{comment}{should call rbfbuildmodel() in order to build a model for you.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7425 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7426 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: dataset added by this function is not saved during model serialization.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7427 \textcolor{comment}{      MODEL ITSELF is serialized, but data used to build it are not.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7428 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7429 \textcolor{comment}{      So, if you 1) add dataset to  empty  RBF  model,  2)  serialize  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7430 \textcolor{comment}{      unserialize it, then you will get an empty RBF model with no dataset}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7431 \textcolor{comment}{      being attached.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7432 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7433 \textcolor{comment}{      From the other side, if you call rbfbuildmodel() between (1) and (2),}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7434 \textcolor{comment}{      then after (2) you will get your fully constructed RBF model  -\/  but}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7435 \textcolor{comment}{      again with no dataset attached, so subsequent calls to rbfbuildmodel()}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7436 \textcolor{comment}{      will produce empty model.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7437 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7438 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7439 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7440 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 20.06.2016 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7441 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7442 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetpointsandscales(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&r, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&xy, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t n, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7443 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetpointsandscales(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&r, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__2d__array}{real\_2d\_array}} \&xy, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1real__1d__array}{real\_1d\_array}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7444 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7445 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7446 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7447 \textcolor{comment}{DEPRECATED:since version 3.11 ALGLIB includes new RBF  model  construction}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7448 \textcolor{comment}{           algorithm, Hierarchical  RBF.  This  algorithm  is  faster  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7449 \textcolor{comment}{           requires less memory than QNN and RBF-\/ML. It is especially good}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7450 \textcolor{comment}{           for large-\/scale interpolation problems. So, we recommend you to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7451 \textcolor{comment}{           consider Hierarchical RBF as default option.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7452 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7453 \textcolor{comment}{==========================================================================}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7454 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7455 \textcolor{comment}{This  function  sets  RBF interpolation algorithm. ALGLIB supports several}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7456 \textcolor{comment}{RBF algorithms with different properties.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7457 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7458 \textcolor{comment}{This algorithm is called RBF-\/QNN and  it  is  good  for  point  sets  with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7459 \textcolor{comment}{following properties:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7460 \textcolor{comment}{a) all points are distinct}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7461 \textcolor{comment}{b) all points are well separated.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7462 \textcolor{comment}{c) points  distribution  is  approximately  uniform.  There is no "{}contour}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7463 \textcolor{comment}{   lines"{}, clusters of points, or other small-\/scale structures.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7464 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7465 \textcolor{comment}{Algorithm description:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7466 \textcolor{comment}{1) interpolation centers are allocated to data points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7467 \textcolor{comment}{2) interpolation radii are calculated as distances to the  nearest centers}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7468 \textcolor{comment}{   times Q coefficient (where Q is a value from [0.75,1.50]).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7469 \textcolor{comment}{3) after  performing (2) radii are transformed in order to avoid situation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7470 \textcolor{comment}{   when single outlier has very large radius and  influences  many  points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7471 \textcolor{comment}{   across all dataset. Transformation has following form:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7472 \textcolor{comment}{       new\_r[i] = min(r[i],Z*median(r[]))}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7473 \textcolor{comment}{   where r[i] is I-\/th radius, median()  is a median  radius across  entire}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7474 \textcolor{comment}{   dataset, Z is user-\/specified value which controls amount  of  deviation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7475 \textcolor{comment}{   from median radius.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7476 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7477 \textcolor{comment}{When (a) is violated,  we  will  be unable to build RBF model. When (b) or}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7478 \textcolor{comment}{(c) are violated, model will be built, but interpolation quality  will  be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7479 \textcolor{comment}{low. See http://www.alglib.net/interpolation/ for more information on this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7480 \textcolor{comment}{subject.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7481 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7482 \textcolor{comment}{This algorithm is used by default.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7483 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7484 \textcolor{comment}{Additional Q parameter controls smoothness properties of the RBF basis:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7485 \textcolor{comment}{* Q<0.75 will give perfectly conditioned basis,  but  terrible  smoothness}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7486 \textcolor{comment}{  properties (RBF interpolant will have sharp peaks around function values)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7487 \textcolor{comment}{* Q around 1.0 gives good balance between smoothness and condition number}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7488 \textcolor{comment}{* Q>1.5 will lead to badly conditioned systems and slow convergence of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7489 \textcolor{comment}{  underlying linear solver (although smoothness will be very good)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7490 \textcolor{comment}{* Q>2.0 will effectively make optimizer useless because it won't  converge}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7491 \textcolor{comment}{  within reasonable amount of iterations. It is possible to set such large}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7492 \textcolor{comment}{  Q, but it is advised not to do so.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7493 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7494 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7495 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model, initialized by RBFCreate() call}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7496 \textcolor{comment}{    Q       -\/   Q parameter, Q>0, recommended value -\/ 1.0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7497 \textcolor{comment}{    Z       -\/   Z parameter, Z>0, recommended value -\/ 5.0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7498 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7499 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE: this   function  has   some   serialization-\/related  subtleties.  We}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7500 \textcolor{comment}{      recommend you to study serialization examples from ALGLIB  Reference}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7501 \textcolor{comment}{      Manual if you want to perform serialization of your models.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7502 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7503 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7504 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7505 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 13.12.2011 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7506 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7507 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetalgoqnn(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} q, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} z, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7508 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetalgoqnn(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7509 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7510 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7511 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7512 \textcolor{comment}{DEPRECATED:since version 3.11 ALGLIB includes new RBF  model  construction}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7513 \textcolor{comment}{           algorithm, Hierarchical  RBF.  This  algorithm  is  faster  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7514 \textcolor{comment}{           requires less memory than QNN and RBF-\/ML. It is especially good}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7515 \textcolor{comment}{           for large-\/scale interpolation problems. So, we recommend you to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7516 \textcolor{comment}{           consider Hierarchical RBF as default option.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7517 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7518 \textcolor{comment}{==========================================================================}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7519 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7520 \textcolor{comment}{This  function  sets  RBF interpolation algorithm. ALGLIB supports several}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7521 \textcolor{comment}{RBF algorithms with different properties.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7522 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7523 \textcolor{comment}{This  algorithm is called RBF-\/ML. It builds  multilayer  RBF  model,  i.e.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7524 \textcolor{comment}{model with subsequently decreasing  radii,  which  allows  us  to  combine}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7525 \textcolor{comment}{smoothness (due to  large radii of  the first layers) with  exactness (due}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7526 \textcolor{comment}{to small radii of the last layers) and fast convergence.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7527 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7528 \textcolor{comment}{Internally RBF-\/ML uses many different  means  of acceleration, from sparse}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7529 \textcolor{comment}{matrices  to  KD-\/trees,  which  results in algorithm whose working time is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7530 \textcolor{comment}{roughly proportional to N*log(N)*Density*RBase\string^2*NLayers,  where  N  is  a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7531 \textcolor{comment}{number of points, Density is an average density if points per unit of  the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7532 \textcolor{comment}{interpolation space, RBase is an initial radius, NLayers is  a  number  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7533 \textcolor{comment}{layers.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7534 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7535 \textcolor{comment}{RBF-\/ML is good for following kinds of interpolation problems:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7536 \textcolor{comment}{1. "{}exact"{} problems (perfect fit) with well separated points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7537 \textcolor{comment}{2. least squares problems with arbitrary distribution of points (algorithm}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7538 \textcolor{comment}{   gives  perfect  fit  where it is possible, and resorts to least squares}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7539 \textcolor{comment}{   fit in the hard areas).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7540 \textcolor{comment}{3. noisy problems where  we  want  to  apply  some  controlled  amount  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7541 \textcolor{comment}{   smoothing.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7542 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7543 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7544 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model, initialized by RBFCreate() call}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7545 \textcolor{comment}{    RBase   -\/   RBase parameter, RBase>0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7546 \textcolor{comment}{    NLayers -\/   NLayers parameter, NLayers>0, recommended value  to  start}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7547 \textcolor{comment}{                with -\/ about 5.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7548 \textcolor{comment}{    LambdaV -\/   regularization value, can be useful when  solving  problem}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7549 \textcolor{comment}{                in the least squares sense.  Optimal  lambda  is  problem-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7550 \textcolor{comment}{                dependent and require trial and error. In our  experience,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7551 \textcolor{comment}{                good lambda can be as large as 0.1, and you can use  0.001}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7552 \textcolor{comment}{                as initial guess.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7553 \textcolor{comment}{                Default  value  -\/ 0.01, which is used when LambdaV is  not}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7554 \textcolor{comment}{                given.  You  can  specify  zero  value,  but  it  is   not}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7555 \textcolor{comment}{                recommended to do so.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7556 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7557 \textcolor{comment}{TUNING ALGORITHM}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7558 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7559 \textcolor{comment}{In order to use this algorithm you have to choose three parameters:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7560 \textcolor{comment}{* initial radius RBase}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7561 \textcolor{comment}{* number of layers in the model NLayers}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7562 \textcolor{comment}{* regularization coefficient LambdaV}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7563 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7564 \textcolor{comment}{Initial radius is easy to choose -\/ you can pick any number  several  times}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7565 \textcolor{comment}{larger  than  the  average  distance between points. Algorithm won't break}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7566 \textcolor{comment}{down if you choose radius which is too large (model construction time will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7567 \textcolor{comment}{increase, but model will be built correctly).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7568 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7569 \textcolor{comment}{Choose such number of layers that RLast=RBase/2\string^(NLayers-\/1)  (radius  used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7570 \textcolor{comment}{by  the  last  layer)  will  be  smaller than the typical distance between}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7571 \textcolor{comment}{points.  In  case  model  error  is  too large, you can increase number of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7572 \textcolor{comment}{layers.  Having  more  layers  will make model construction and evaluation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7573 \textcolor{comment}{proportionally slower, but it will allow you to have model which precisely}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7574 \textcolor{comment}{fits your data. From the other side, if you want to  suppress  noise,  you}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7575 \textcolor{comment}{can DECREASE number of layers to make your model less flexible.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7576 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7577 \textcolor{comment}{Regularization coefficient LambdaV controls smoothness of  the  individual}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7578 \textcolor{comment}{models built for each layer. We recommend you to use default value in case}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7579 \textcolor{comment}{you don't want to tune this parameter,  because  having  non-\/zero  LambdaV}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7580 \textcolor{comment}{accelerates and stabilizes internal iterative algorithm. In case you  want}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7581 \textcolor{comment}{to suppress noise you can use  LambdaV  as  additional  parameter  (larger}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7582 \textcolor{comment}{value = more smoothness) to tune.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7583 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7584 \textcolor{comment}{TYPICAL ERRORS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7585 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7586 \textcolor{comment}{1. Using  initial  radius  which is too large. Memory requirements  of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7587 \textcolor{comment}{   RBF-\/ML are roughly proportional to N*Density*RBase\string^2 (where Density  is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7588 \textcolor{comment}{   an average density of points per unit of the interpolation  space).  In}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7589 \textcolor{comment}{   the extreme case of the very large RBase we will need O(N\string^2)  units  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7590 \textcolor{comment}{   memory -\/ and many layers in order to decrease radius to some reasonably}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7591 \textcolor{comment}{   small value.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7592 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7593 \textcolor{comment}{2. Using too small number of layers -\/ RBF models with large radius are not}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7594 \textcolor{comment}{   flexible enough to reproduce small variations in the  target  function.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7595 \textcolor{comment}{   You  need  many  layers  with  different radii, from large to small, in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7596 \textcolor{comment}{   order to have good model.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7597 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7598 \textcolor{comment}{3. Using  initial  radius  which  is  too  small.  You will get model with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7599 \textcolor{comment}{   "{}holes"{} in the areas which are too far away from interpolation centers.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7600 \textcolor{comment}{   However, algorithm will work correctly (and quickly) in this case.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7601 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7602 \textcolor{comment}{4. Using too many layers -\/ you will get too large and too slow model. This}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7603 \textcolor{comment}{   model  will  perfectly  reproduce  your function, but maybe you will be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7604 \textcolor{comment}{   able to achieve similar results with less layers (and less memory).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7605 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7606 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7607 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 02.03.2012 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7608 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7609 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetalgomultilayer(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} rbase, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nlayers, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} lambdav, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7610 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetalgomultilayer(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} rbase, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nlayers, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7611 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7612 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7613 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7614 \textcolor{comment}{This  function  sets  RBF interpolation algorithm. ALGLIB supports several}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7615 \textcolor{comment}{RBF algorithms with different properties.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7616 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7617 \textcolor{comment}{This  algorithm is called Hierarchical RBF. It  similar  to  its  previous}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7618 \textcolor{comment}{incarnation, RBF-\/ML, i.e.  it  also  builds  a  sequence  of  models  with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7619 \textcolor{comment}{decreasing radii. However, it uses more economical way of  building  upper}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7620 \textcolor{comment}{layers (ones with large radii), which results in faster model construction}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7621 \textcolor{comment}{and evaluation, as well as smaller memory footprint during construction.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7622 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7623 \textcolor{comment}{This algorithm has following important features:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7624 \textcolor{comment}{* ability to handle millions of points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7625 \textcolor{comment}{* controllable smoothing via nonlinearity penalization}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7626 \textcolor{comment}{* support for NX-\/dimensional models with NX=1 or NX>3 (unlike QNN or RBF-\/ML)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7627 \textcolor{comment}{* support for specification of per-\/dimensional  radii  via  scale  vector,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7628 \textcolor{comment}{  which is set by means of rbfsetpointsandscales() function. This  feature}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7629 \textcolor{comment}{  is useful if you solve  spatio-\/temporal  interpolation  problems,  where}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7630 \textcolor{comment}{  different radii are required for spatial and temporal dimensions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7631 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7632 \textcolor{comment}{Running times are roughly proportional to:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7633 \textcolor{comment}{* N*log(N)*NLayers -\/ for model construction}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7634 \textcolor{comment}{* N*NLayers -\/ for model evaluation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7635 \textcolor{comment}{You may see that running time does not depend on search radius  or  points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7636 \textcolor{comment}{density, just on number of layers in the hierarchy.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7637 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7638 \textcolor{comment}{IMPORTANT: this model construction algorithm was introduced in ALGLIB 3.11}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7639 \textcolor{comment}{           and  produces  models  which  are  INCOMPATIBLE  with  previous}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7640 \textcolor{comment}{           versions of ALGLIB. You can  not  unserialize  models  produced}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7641 \textcolor{comment}{           with this function in ALGLIB 3.10 or earlier.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7642 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7643 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7644 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model, initialized by rbfcreate() call}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7645 \textcolor{comment}{    RBase   -\/   RBase parameter, RBase>0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7646 \textcolor{comment}{    NLayers -\/   NLayers parameter, NLayers>0, recommended value  to  start}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7647 \textcolor{comment}{                with -\/ about 5.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7648 \textcolor{comment}{    LambdaNS-\/   >=0, nonlinearity penalty coefficient, negative values are}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7649 \textcolor{comment}{                not allowed. This parameter adds controllable smoothing to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7650 \textcolor{comment}{                the problem, which may reduce noise. Specification of non-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7651 \textcolor{comment}{                zero lambda means that in addition to fitting error solver}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7652 \textcolor{comment}{                will  also  minimize   LambdaNS*|S''(x)|\string^2  (appropriately}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7653 \textcolor{comment}{                generalized to multiple dimensions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7654 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7655 \textcolor{comment}{                Specification of exactly zero value means that no  penalty}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7656 \textcolor{comment}{                is added  (we  do  not  even  evaluate  matrix  of  second}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7657 \textcolor{comment}{                derivatives which is necessary for smoothing).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7658 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7659 \textcolor{comment}{                Calculation of nonlinearity penalty is costly -\/ it results}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7660 \textcolor{comment}{                in  several-\/fold  increase  of  model  construction  time.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7661 \textcolor{comment}{                Evaluation time remains the same.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7662 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7663 \textcolor{comment}{                Optimal  lambda  is  problem-\/dependent and requires  trial}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7664 \textcolor{comment}{                and  error.  Good  value to  start  from  is  1e-\/5...1e-\/6,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7665 \textcolor{comment}{                which corresponds to slightly noticeable smoothing  of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7666 \textcolor{comment}{                function.  Value  1e-\/2  usually  means  that  quite  heavy}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7667 \textcolor{comment}{                smoothing is applied.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7668 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7669 \textcolor{comment}{TUNING ALGORITHM}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7670 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7671 \textcolor{comment}{In order to use this algorithm you have to choose three parameters:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7672 \textcolor{comment}{* initial radius RBase}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7673 \textcolor{comment}{* number of layers in the model NLayers}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7674 \textcolor{comment}{* penalty coefficient LambdaNS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7675 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7676 \textcolor{comment}{Initial radius is easy to choose -\/ you can pick any number  several  times}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7677 \textcolor{comment}{larger  than  the  average  distance between points. Algorithm won't break}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7678 \textcolor{comment}{down if you choose radius which is too large (model construction time will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7679 \textcolor{comment}{increase, but model will be built correctly).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7680 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7681 \textcolor{comment}{Choose such number of layers that RLast=RBase/2\string^(NLayers-\/1)  (radius  used}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7682 \textcolor{comment}{by  the  last  layer)  will  be  smaller than the typical distance between}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7683 \textcolor{comment}{points.  In  case  model  error  is  too large, you can increase number of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7684 \textcolor{comment}{layers.  Having  more  layers  will make model construction and evaluation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7685 \textcolor{comment}{proportionally slower, but it will allow you to have model which precisely}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7686 \textcolor{comment}{fits your data. From the other side, if you want to  suppress  noise,  you}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7687 \textcolor{comment}{can DECREASE number of layers to make your model less flexible (or specify}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7688 \textcolor{comment}{non-\/zero LambdaNS).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7689 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7690 \textcolor{comment}{TYPICAL ERRORS}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7691 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7692 \textcolor{comment}{1. Using too small number of layers -\/ RBF models with large radius are not}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7693 \textcolor{comment}{   flexible enough to reproduce small variations in the  target  function.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7694 \textcolor{comment}{   You  need  many  layers  with  different radii, from large to small, in}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7695 \textcolor{comment}{   order to have good model.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7696 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7697 \textcolor{comment}{2. Using  initial  radius  which  is  too  small.  You will get model with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7698 \textcolor{comment}{   "{}holes"{} in the areas which are too far away from interpolation centers.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7699 \textcolor{comment}{   However, algorithm will work correctly (and quickly) in this case.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7700 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7701 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7702 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 20.06.2016 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7703 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7704 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetalgohierarchical(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} rbase, \textcolor{keyword}{const} ae\_int\_t nlayers, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} lambdans, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}

\DoxyCodeLine{7795 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7796 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7797 \textcolor{comment}{This function sets support radius parameter  of  hierarchical  (version 2)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7798 \textcolor{comment}{RBF constructor.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7799 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7800 \textcolor{comment}{Hierarchical RBF model achieves great speed-\/up  by removing from the model}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7801 \textcolor{comment}{excessive (too dense) nodes. Say, if you have RBF radius equal to 1 meter,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7802 \textcolor{comment}{and two nodes are just 1 millimeter apart, you  may  remove  one  of  them}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7803 \textcolor{comment}{without reducing model quality.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7804 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7805 \textcolor{comment}{Support radius parameter is used to justify which points need removal, and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7806 \textcolor{comment}{which do not. If two points are less than  SUPPORT\_R*CUR\_RADIUS  units  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7807 \textcolor{comment}{distance apart, one of them is removed from the model. The larger  support}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7808 \textcolor{comment}{radius  is, the faster model  construction  AND  evaluation are.  However,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7809 \textcolor{comment}{too large values result in "{}bumpy"{} models.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7810 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7811 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7812 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model, initialized by RBFCreate() call}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7813 \textcolor{comment}{    R       -\/   support radius coefficient, >=0.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7814 \textcolor{comment}{                Recommended values are [0.1,0.4] range, with 0.1 being}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7815 \textcolor{comment}{                default value.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7816 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7817 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7818 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 01.02.2017 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7819 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7820 \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} rbfsetv2supportr(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{classalglib_1_1rbfmodel}{rbfmodel}} \&s, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} r, \textcolor{keyword}{const} \mbox{\hyperlink{structalglib_1_1xparams}{xparams}} \_xparams = alglib::xdefault);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7821 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7822 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7823 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7824 \textcolor{comment}{This   function  builds  RBF  model  and  returns  report  (contains  some}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7825 \textcolor{comment}{information which can be used for evaluation of the algorithm properties).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7826 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7827 \textcolor{comment}{Call to this function modifies RBF model by calculating its centers/radii/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7828 \textcolor{comment}{weights  and  saving  them  into  RBFModel  structure.  Initially RBFModel}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7829 \textcolor{comment}{contain zero coefficients, but after call to this function  we  will  have}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7830 \textcolor{comment}{coefficients which were calculated in order to fit our dataset.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7831 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7832 \textcolor{comment}{After you called this function you can call RBFCalc(),  RBFGridCalc()  and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7833 \textcolor{comment}{other model calculation functions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7834 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7835 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7836 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model, initialized by RBFCreate() call}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7837 \textcolor{comment}{    Rep     -\/   report:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7838 \textcolor{comment}{                * Rep.TerminationType:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7839 \textcolor{comment}{                  * -\/5 -\/ non-\/distinct basis function centers were detected,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7840 \textcolor{comment}{                         interpolation  aborted;  only  QNN  returns  this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7841 \textcolor{comment}{                         error   code, other  algorithms  can  handle non-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7842 \textcolor{comment}{                         distinct nodes.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7843 \textcolor{comment}{                  * -\/4 -\/ nonconvergence of the internal SVD solver}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7844 \textcolor{comment}{                  * -\/3   incorrect model construction algorithm was chosen:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7845 \textcolor{comment}{                         QNN or RBF-\/ML, combined with one of the incompatible}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7846 \textcolor{comment}{                         features -\/ NX=1 or NX>3; points with per-\/dimension}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7847 \textcolor{comment}{                         scales.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7848 \textcolor{comment}{                  *  1 -\/ successful termination}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7849 \textcolor{comment}{                  *  8 -\/ a termination request was submitted via}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7850 \textcolor{comment}{                         rbfrequesttermination() function.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7851 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7852 \textcolor{comment}{                Fields which are set only by modern RBF solvers (hierarchical}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7853 \textcolor{comment}{                or nonnegative; older solvers like QNN and ML initialize these}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7854 \textcolor{comment}{                fields by NANs):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7855 \textcolor{comment}{                * rep.rmserror -\/ root-\/mean-\/square error at nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7856 \textcolor{comment}{                * rep.maxerror -\/ maximum error at nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7857 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7858 \textcolor{comment}{                Fields are used for debugging purposes:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7859 \textcolor{comment}{                * Rep.IterationsCount -\/ iterations count of the LSQR solver}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7860 \textcolor{comment}{                * Rep.NMV -\/ number of matrix-\/vector products}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7861 \textcolor{comment}{                * Rep.ARows -\/ rows count for the system matrix}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7862 \textcolor{comment}{                * Rep.ACols -\/ columns count for the system matrix}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7863 \textcolor{comment}{                * Rep.ANNZ -\/ number of significantly non-\/zero elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7864 \textcolor{comment}{                  (elements above some algorithm-\/determined threshold)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7865 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7866 \textcolor{comment}{NOTE:  failure  to  build  model will leave current state of the structure}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7867 \textcolor{comment}{unchanged.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7868 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7869 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7870 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 13.12.2011 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7871 \textcolor{comment}{*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{7978 \textcolor{comment}{/*************************************************************************}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7979 \textcolor{comment}{This function calculates values of the RBF model at the given point.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7980 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7981 \textcolor{comment}{This is general function which can be used for arbitrary NX (dimension  of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7982 \textcolor{comment}{the space of arguments) and NY (dimension of the function itself). However}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7983 \textcolor{comment}{when  you  have  NY=1  you  may  find more convenient to use rbfcalc2() or}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7984 \textcolor{comment}{rbfcalc3().}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7985 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7986 \textcolor{comment}{If you want to perform parallel model evaluation  from  multiple  threads,}}

\DoxyCodeLine{7988 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7989 \textcolor{comment}{This function returns 0.0 when model is not initialized.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7990 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7991 \textcolor{comment}{INPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7992 \textcolor{comment}{    S       -\/   RBF model}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7993 \textcolor{comment}{    X       -\/   coordinates, array[NX].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7994 \textcolor{comment}{                X may have more than NX elements, in this case only}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7995 \textcolor{comment}{                leading NX will be used.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7996 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7997 \textcolor{comment}{OUTPUT PARAMETERS:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7998 \textcolor{comment}{    Y       -\/   function value, array[NY]. Y is out-\/parameter and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7999 \textcolor{comment}{                reallocated after call to this function. In case you  want}}
\DoxyCodeLine{8000 \textcolor{comment}{                to reuse previously allocated Y, you may use RBFCalcBuf(),}}
\DoxyCodeLine{8001 \textcolor{comment}{                which reallocates Y only when it is too small.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{8002 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{8003 \textcolor{comment}{  -\/-\/ ALGLIB -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{8004 \textcolor{comment}{     Copyright 13.12.2011 by Bochkanov Sergey}}
